Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Sunnah of Lengthening, Du'a, and Individual Prayer in Eclipse Prayer
Sunnah practices for eclipse prayer: lengthening, du'a, and individual prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the sunnah of lengthening in eclipse prayer and explain the etiquette of du'a and individual prayer when the imam is absent.

Core Idea
Lengthen the rak'ahs, bowings, prostrations; after prayer, imam makes du'a until eclipse clears; if no imam, pray individually.

Having covered the basic form, we now turn to the recommended practices that complete the eclipse prayer. The text instructs us to lengthen the prayer, following the Prophet's example, and then to engage in supplication until the eclipse ends. It also addresses the situation when an imam is not available.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnah of lengthening
The text states that it is sunnah to lengthen the two rak'ahs, as well as their bowings and prostrations. The hadith of Aisha describes the Prophet's long recitation, long bowing, and long prostration.
Lengthening should be proportionate to the duration of the eclipse.
2
Describe the du'a after prayer
After the prayer, the imam leads du'a, either sitting facing the qiblah or standing facing the people. The congregation says Ameen. The du'a continues until the eclipse clears.
The preferred position is standing facing the people.
3
Address the absence of an imam
If the imam is not present, people should pray individually. The commentary notes that this is not wajib but recommended to avoid disunity.
Individual prayer is still sunnah; congregation is not a condition.
4
Connect to the proofs
The proofs include the hadith of Aisha for lengthening, and the hadiths of Abu Musa and Abu Hurayrah for du'a and remembrance.

وجه : (۱) حدیث میں ہے ۔ عن ابی موسی قال خسفت الشمس في زمن النبي علي .... قال ان هذه الآيات التي يرسل الله لا تكون لموت احد ولا لحياته و لكن الله يرسلها يخوف بها عباده فاذا رأيتم منها شيئا فافزعوا الی ذکره و دعائه و استغفاره - (مسلم شریف ، باب ذکر النداء بصلاة الكسوف الصلاة جامعة ،ص ۱۳۶۹، نمبر ۱۹۱۲ ۲۱۱۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ اس قسم کی خوف کی چیز ہو تو دعا اور استغفار میں مشغول ہونا چاہئے (۲) عن ابي هريرة ...... فقال ان الشمس والقمر آيتان من آيت الله وانهما لا يخسفان لموت احد فاذا كان ذلك فصلوا وادعوا حتى يكشف ما بكم ( بخاری شریف ، باب الصلوۃ فی کسوف القمر ص ۱۴۵ نمبر ۱۰۶۳ر مسلم شریف ، باب ذکر النداء بصلاة الكسوف، الصلاة جامعة ،ص ۱۳۶۹، نمبر ۲۱۲۲/۹۱۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ نماز پڑھو اور اس وقت تک دعا کرتے رہو جب تک گرہن ختم نہ ہو ترجمه : (۸۴۱) اگر امام موجود نہ ہو تو لوگ اکیلے نماز پڑھیں۔ تشریح : امام نہ ہو تو الگ الگ پڑھنا واجب نہیں ہے، بلکہ یہ مصلحت کا تقاضا ہے،اس لئے اگر انتشار کا خطرہ نہ ہو تو یہ سب
Chapter on the Eclipse Prayer. There is no adhan, no iqamah, no khutbah, and recitation is silent, not aloud. Evidence: (1) From Abu Bakrah... (hadith). From this hadith it is understood that the prayer at the time of solar eclipse is sunnah, and there is no mention of two bowings in it, therefore there will not be two bowings in one rak'ah. Also there is no mention of adhan and iqamah, and there is no formal khutbah like Jumu'ah and the two Eids. (2) From Qabisah al-Hilali... (hadith). In this hadith, just as the Fajr prayer is prayed with one bowing, similarly the eclipse prayer will be prayed. 'Ahadath salatin min al-maktubah' refers to Fajr prayer. Also no mention of two bowings. (3) Long hadith of Samurah ibn Jundub... (hadith). This hadith also mentions that two bowings were not performed in one rak'ah. It also shows that recitation is silent. (4) From Ibn Abbas... (hadith). In this hadith, not a single letter of Quran was heard, meaning recitation in eclipse prayer is silent. (5) The announcement is made by saying 'Al-salat jami'ah'. The hadith of Ibn Umar says that 'Al-salat jami'ah' was called. (839) It is sunnah to lengthen them (the two rak'ahs) and to lengthen their bowings and prostrations. (840) Then the imam makes du'a, sitting facing the qiblah if he wishes, or standing facing the people, and that is better, and they say Ameen to his du'a until the eclipse clears. Lexicon: al-kusuf means solar eclipse; al-khusuf means lunar eclipse; al-ifza' means fear, panic. At that time, prayer is sunnah. Translation: (839) It is sunnah to lengthen both rak'ahs and to lengthen their bowings and prostrations. Commentary: It is sunnah that the eclipse prayer be long, with long bowings and prostrations until the sun clears. Evidence: (a) Aisha... (hadith). This hadith mentions the prayer being long. Translation: (840) Then the imam makes du'a, sitting facing the qiblah if he wishes, or standing facing the people, and that is better, and they say Ameen to his du'a until the sun clears. Commentary: After the prayer, he makes du'a. There are two forms: (1) sitting facing the qiblah and making du'a for the people, (2) facing the people and making du'a standing, which is better. Evidence: (1) Hadith of Abu Musa... (hadith) indicates that when such a fearful thing occurs, one should engage in du'a and istighfar. (2) Hadith of Abu Hurayrah... (hadith) says pray and make du'a until it is cleared. Translation: (841) If the imam is not present, the people pray individually. Commentary: When the imam is absent, praying individually is not wajib, but it is required by maslahah; therefore if there is no risk of disunity, all.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof from the chapter on Salat al-Kusuf (eclipse prayer). It begins by stating the foundational rulings: no adhan, no iqamah, no khutbah, and silent recitation. The author then provides five hadith proofs. The first hadith from Abu Bakrah establishes the sunnah nature and shows that only two rak'ahs are prayed with one bowing per rak'ah; no double bowing. The second from Qabisah confirms a single bowing by analogy to Fajr. The third from Samurah similarly affirms silent recitation and one bowing. The fourth from Ibn Abbas directly shows silent recitation. The fifth from Ibn Umar shows the call 'Al-salat jami'ah'. Next, ruling 839 states that lengthening the rak'ahs, bowings, and prostrations is sunnah, supported by Aisha's hadith of the Prophet's long prayer. Ruling 840 describes the imam's du'a after prayer: he may sit facing qiblah or stand facing the people (preferred), and the congregation says Ameen until the eclipse ends. Evidence from Abu Musa and Abu Hurayrah encourages du'a and remembrance. Finally, ruling 841 says if the imam is absent, people pray individually; the commentary clarifies this is not obligatory but recommended to avoid disunity.

Key Terms
الكسوف (al-kusuf): Solar eclipse; the sun's light being obscured.
الخسوف (al-khusuf): Lunar eclipse; the moon's light being obscured.
الصلاة جامعة (al-salat jami'ah): The call to gather for eclipse prayer, distinguished from adhan.
سنة (sunnah): In this context, a recommended act that the Prophet performed and encouraged.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is true about the du'a after Salat al-Kusuf?
A) The imam must face the qiblah while sitting.
B) The imam must stand facing the people.
C) The imam may do either, but standing facing the people is better.
D) The congregation remains silent during du'a.

Key Takeaway
Lengthening the eclipse prayer and supplicating until the eclipse ends are sunnah, and if no imam is present, each person prays individually.

Lengthening the Solar Eclipse Prayer: Ruling and Proof
Ruling with proof on lengthening eclipse prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that lengthening the solar eclipse prayer is sunnah muakkadah in the Hanafi school and explain the proof from the hadith of Aisha.

Core Idea
Lengthening the eclipse prayer is sunnah, not wajib, based on the Prophet's consistent practice.

The solar eclipse prayer (salat al-kusuf) is a sunnah prayer performed during a solar eclipse. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that it is sunnah muakkadah to lengthen this prayer, including its recitation, bowing, and prostration. We will explore the primary evidence from the hadith of Aisha and understand why this ruling is classified as sunnah rather than wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage clearly states: 'It is sunnah to lengthen both rak'ahs and to lengthen their bowings and prostrations.' Identify the act (tatwil of eclipse prayer) and its hukm (sunnah muakkadah).
Sunnah muakkadah is an emphasized sunnah; omitting it is disliked but not sinful.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Aisha (RA) describing the Prophet's (PBUH) prayer during a solar eclipse. Identify the source as an ahad hadith with zanni thubut.
The hadith is found in Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly describes the Prophet lengthening each part (recitation, bowing, prostration). This indicates the recommended nature of lengthening. The Hanafi school derives sunnah from prophetic action combined with the absence of an explicit command.
If it were wajib, the Prophet would have commanded it explicitly.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider lengthening to be recommended but may have different details. The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih, but the Hanafi position is mufta bihi within the school.
The difference is in degree of emphasis, not in the basic act.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the specific prophetic practice as reported in authentic ahadith. Since there is no textual command making it wajib, it remains sunnah. The authority weight is zahir riwayah.
The mufta bihi is that lengthening is sunnah muakkadah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَسُنَّ تَطْوِيلُهُمَا وَتَطْوِيلُ رُكُوعِهِمَا وَسُجُودِهِمَا. عَنْ عَائِشَةَ زَوْجِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ أَخْبَرَتْهُ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ صَلَّى يَوْمَ خَسَفَتِ الشَّمْسُ فَقَامَ فَكَبَّرَ فَقَرَأَ قِرَاءَةً طَوِيلَةً ثُمَّ رَكَعَ رُكُوعًا طَوِيلًا ثُمَّ رَفَعَ رَأْسَهُ فَقَالَ سَمِعَ اللَّهُ لِمَنْ حَمِدَهُ وَقَامَ كَمَا هُوَ ثُمَّ قَرَأَ قِرَاءَةً طَوِيلَةً وَهِيَ أَدْنَى مِنَ الْقِرَاءَةِ الْأُولَى ثُمَّ رَكَعَ رُكُوعًا طَوِيلًا وَهِيَ أَدْنَى مِنَ الرَّكْعَةِ الْأُولَى ثُمَّ سَجَدَ سُجُودًا طَوِيلًا ثُمَّ فَعَلَ فِي الرَّكْعَةِ الْآخِرَةِ مِثْلَ ذَلِكَ ثُمَّ سَلَّمَ وَقَدْ تَجَلَّتِ الشَّمْسُ.
It is sunnah to lengthen both rak'ahs and to lengthen their bowings and prostrations. From Aisha, wife of the Prophet (peace be upon him), she informed him that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) prayed on the day the sun eclipsed: he stood and said the takbir, then recited a long recitation, then bowed a long bowing, then raised his head saying 'Allah hears whoever praises Him', and stood as he was, then recited a long recitation which was shorter than the first recitation, then bowed a long bowing which was shorter than the first bowing, then prostrated a long prostration, then did the same in the last rak'ah, then said the salam while the sun had cleared.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states that it is sunnah (recommended) to lengthen the solar eclipse prayer (salat al-kusuf) in both rak'ahs, including the recitation, bowing, and prostration. The proof is the hadith of Aisha describing the Prophet's practice during a solar eclipse. The Hanafi school follows this sunnah, emphasizing that the prayer should be prolonged until the eclipse ends, as indicated by the hadith. The length of recitation in the second rak'ah should be somewhat shorter than the first.

Key Terms
سُنَّة (sunnah): A recommended act; omission does not incur sin but doing it gains reward.
الكسوف (al-kusuf): Solar eclipse.
تطويل (tatwil): Lengthening or prolonging the prayer and its parts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the hukm of lengthening the solar eclipse prayer in the Hanafi school?
A) Wajib
B) Sunnah muakkadah
C) Fard
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Lengthening the solar eclipse prayer is an emphasized sunnah (sunnah muakkadah) in the Hanafi school, based on the Prophet's practice as narrated by Aisha.

The Post-Eclipse Supplication: A Sunnah Act
Ruling on supplication after eclipse prayer with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on supplication after the eclipse prayer and identify the key elements of its performance and proof.

Core Idea
Dua after eclipse prayer is a sunnah, not wajib — the imam leads it until the phenomenon ends.

The eclipse prayer (salat al-kusuf) includes more than just the unique bowing and prostration. After the salam, the imam turns to supplication. Our source passage describes how the imam makes dua, the congregation says Ameen, and this continues until the eclipse clears. The ruling is sunnah, grounded in prophetic instruction to hasten to remembrance and supplication during such signs of Allah’s power.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage describes the imam making dua after the eclipse prayer. Determine the legal status: is it wajib, sunnah, or mubah? The Hanafi school classifies it as sunnah (recommended, not obligatory).
Sunnah means the Prophet (peace be upon him) did it or encouraged it, but omission is not sinful.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
Find the hadith evidence cited. The text quotes hadiths from Abu Musa and Abu Huraira that command turning to remembrance, supplication, and prayer during eclipses.
The dalil is ahad (single-transmitter) hadith, so its thubut is zanni, not qat'i.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (indication)
How does the hadith specifically support the act described? The command 'hasten to His remembrance, supplication, and seeking forgiveness' indicates desirability (istihbab), not obligation, because the context is fear and turning to Allah, and the command is general.
Hadiths use imperative forms but here they indicate recommendation due to accompanying factors.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (scholarly difference)
Some schools (e.g., some Shafi'is) do not specify a separate supplication after the eclipse prayer, though they agree on dua during the event. The Hanafi position is that a dedicated post-prayer dua is sunnah.
The practical difference (thamarah) is that Hanafis prolong the dua after prayer; others may not.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The Zahir al-Riwayah position is that the supplication is sunnah. Later Hanafi fatwa works uphold this. The imam may choose to sit facing qibla or stand facing the congregation; standing is better.
The crowd says Ameen loudly during the imam's dua (ta'min).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ يَدْعُو الإِمَامُ جَالِسًا مُسْتَقْبِلَ الْقِبْلَةِ إِنْ شَاءَ أَوْ قَائِمًا مُسْتَقْبِلَ النَّاسِ وَهُوَ أَحْسَنُ وَيُؤَمِّنُونَ عَلَى دُعَائِهِ حَتَّى يَكْمُلَ انْجِلَاءُ الشَّمْسِ. عَنْ أَبِي مُوسَى قَالَ: خَسَفَتِ الشَّمْسُ فِي زَمَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ ... قَالَ: إِنَّ هَذِهِ الآيَاتِ الَّتِي يُرْسِلُ اللَّهُ لاَ تَكُونُ لِمَوْتِ أَحَدٍ وَلاَ لِحَيَاتِهِ وَلَكِنَّ اللَّهَ يُرْسِلُهَا يُخَوِّفُ بِهَا عِبَادَهُ فَإِذَا رَأَيْتُمْ مِنْهَا شَيْئًا فَافْزَعُوا إِلَى ذِكْرِهِ وَدُعَائِهِ وَاسْتِغْفَارِهِ. عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ ... أَنَّ الشَّمْسَ وَالْقَمَرَ آيَتَانِ مِنْ آيَاتِ اللَّهِ وَأَنَّهُمَا لاَ يَخْسِفَانِ لِمَوْتِ أَحَدٍ فَإِذَا كَانَ ذَلِكَ فَصَلُّوا وَادْعُوا حَتَّى يُكْشَفَ مَا بِكُمْ.
Then the imam makes supplication, sitting facing the qibla if he wishes, or standing facing the people, and that is better, and they say 'Ameen' to his supplication until the sun completes clearing. From Abu Musa: The sun eclipsed in the time of the Prophet (peace be upon him)... he said: 'These signs that Allah sends are not for the death of anyone nor for his life, but Allah sends them to frighten His servants. So when you see anything of them, hasten to His remembrance, supplication, and seeking forgiveness.' From Abu Huraira: 'The sun and the moon are two signs from Allah's signs, and they do not eclipse for the death of anyone. So when that happens, pray and supplicate until what is upon you is removed.'
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. After the eclipse prayer, the imam engages in supplication (dua). He has two options: sitting facing the qibla, or standing facing the congregation; the latter is considered better. The congregation responds with Ameen. This continues until the eclipse ends. The proof is from hadiths that command turning to Allah in supplication and remembrance during eclipses and other frightening natural phenomena. The Hanafi school upholds this as a recommended practice.

Key Terms
دعاء (du'a): Supplication, a form of worship invoking Allah.
تأمين (ta'min): Saying 'Ameen' after the imam's supplication.
انجلاء (injila'): Clearing of the eclipse; the sun or moon returning to normal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Standing facing the congregation
C) Sitting facing the congregation
D) Standing facing the qibla

Key Takeaway
The post-eclipse supplication is a sunnah act in the Hanafi school, performed by the imam with the congregation saying Ameen until the eclipse ends.

Praying Individually for Eclipses and Natural Phenomena
Ruling on praying individually when imam absent or for other signs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying individually for eclipses and terrifying natural phenomena when the imam is absent and identify the conditions that trigger this ruling.

Core Idea
When the imam is absent, eclipse and natural disaster prayers are performed individually to avoid disorder.

This lesson examines a short but important passage from classical Hanafi fiqh regarding prayers during natural phenomena like eclipses, terrifying darkness, strong winds, and general fear. The ruling is straightforward: if the imam is not present, you pray individually. But why does the Hanafi school recommend this, and what are the practical implications? Let us break down the legal reasoning and application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The passage gives a ruling for a specific act: the prayer (salat) performed during eclipses and other terrifying natural signs. First, note that the default ruling for this prayer is not congregational obligation but a recommended sunnah, and the text specifies when it becomes individual.
The default eclipse prayer in Hanafi is sunnah mu'akkadah in congregation when the imam is present.
2
Recognize the condition that changes the ruling
The key phrase is 'if the imam is not present.' This condition triggers the shift from congregational sunnah to individual (furada). The absence of the imam is the decisive factor.
The imam here refers to the sultan or the government-appointed imam, not just any prayer leader.
3
List the examples given in the text
The passage lists specific phenomena: lunar eclipse (khusuf), terrifying darkness during the day, strong wind, and fear (faza'). These are all cases where the same ruling applies.
Solar eclipse (kusuf) is also included by analogy, though the text only mentions lunar eclipse.
4
Understand the rationale behind the ruling
The Hanafi school prioritizes individual prayer in these situations to avoid disorder (fitna) and chaos. Gathering a large congregation when people are already frightened may lead to panic. Thus, individual prayer is more suitable.
This reflects the Hanafi principle of considering public interest (maslahah) in avoiding harm.
5
Apply the ruling to a practical scenario
Now practice: if a solar eclipse occurs at a time when the local imam is on travel, what should the community do? According to this passage, they should pray individually, not attempt to form a congregation.
If the imam is present, the congregation is recommended; if absent, individual prayer is the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ لَمْ يَحْضُرِ الإِمَامُ صَلَّوْا فُرَادَى. كَالْخُسُوفِ وَالظُّلْمَةِ الْهَائِلَةِ نَهَارًا وَالرِّيحِ الشَّدِيدَةِ وَالْفَزَعِ.
And if the imam is not present, they pray individually. Like the lunar eclipse, terrifying darkness during the day, strong wind, and fear.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This is a ruling statement specifying that for solar eclipse, and similarly for lunar eclipse, terrifying darkness, strong wind, and other frightening natural phenomena, the prayer should be performed individually (furada) if the imam is not present. The Hanafi school considers congregational prayer for eclipses as sunnah when the imam is present, but if he is absent or there is risk of disorder (fitna), then praying individually is recommended. The proofs from hadith encourage hastening to prayer and supplication during such events, and the Hanafi jurisprudence applies this to maintain order.

Key Terms
فرادى (furada): Individually, alone, not in congregation.
الخسوف (al-khusuf): Lunar eclipse.
الهائلة (al-ha'ila): Terrifying, frightening.
الفزع (al-faza'): Fear, panic, especially from natural phenomena.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When the imam is present
B) During a lunar eclipse only
C) When the imam is absent or for terrifying natural signs
D) Never; it must always be in congregation

Key Takeaway
Eclipse and natural disaster prayers are performed individually if the imam is absent, to maintain order.

Definition and Ruling of Istisqa' (Prayer for Rain)
Definition and basic ruling of istisqa'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define istisqa' and state the Hanafi ruling that salat al-istisqa' is sunnah muakkadah, while also knowing the position of Imam Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
Istisqa' is seeking rain; the Hanafi school holds the prayer as sunnah, but dua alone suffices.

This lesson introduces the chapter on istisqa' (prayer for rain). Although the Arabic text is only the chapter heading, the Urdu commentary clarifies that istisqa' means seeking rain from Allah. The Hanafi school has an important internal difference: Imam Abu Hanifa considered the prayer unnecessary, but later scholars elevated it to sunnah muakkadah. Understanding this development is key to proper fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Parse the term istisqa'
Break down the word: istisqa' is derived from saqa (to give water). It means seeking rain from Allah through prayer or supplication.
2
Identify the legal ruling
From the commentary, identify the ruling: salat al-istisqa' is sunnah muakkadah according to the majority of Hanafi scholars, though Imam Abu Hanifa himself did not require a special prayer.
3
Recognize the intra-madhhab difference
Note the difference between Imam Abu Hanifa's view and his students. This is a classic example of usul affecting furu': Abu Hanifa's strict reliance on certain hadith vs. the Sahibayn's acceptance of other evidence.
4
Apply the mufta bihi
The mufta bihi is that the prayer is sunnah muakkadah. This is the position for fatwa, following the later Hanafi scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الاستسقاء

Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This is the opening of a new chapter on the prayer for rain (salat al-istisqa'). The text contains only the chapter heading in Arabic, but the Urdu commentary provides important context: istisqa' means seeking rain. Imam Abu Hanifa's view is that performing a specific prayer is not necessary; one can simply make dua. However, later in the Hanafi school, the prayer is considered sunnah. The full ruling is not given here, as the page cuts off.

Praying Individually During Eclipses and Calamities
Ruling on individual prayer during calamities when imam absent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing prayer individually during eclipses and terrifying phenomena when the imam is absent, and identify the specific situations that require individual prayer.

Core Idea
When no imam is present, pray individually during eclipses and terror to avoid chaos.

Natural calamities like eclipses, terrifying darkness, and strong winds can cause panic. The Hanafi school addresses how to perform prayer during such events: if the imam is present, he leads a congregation; but if he is absent, individual prayer is prescribed to prevent disorder. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is performing prayer during eclipses and terrifying phenomena. The ruling: if the imam is present, congregation; if absent, pray individually.
The text primarily focuses on the scenario without imam.
2
List the specific cases
The cases mentioned are: solar eclipse, lunar eclipse, terrifying daytime darkness, strong wind, and panic (faza‘).
These are events that inspire fear and potential chaos.
3
Understand the rationale
The reason for individual prayer is to avoid chaos (iftiraq) and shouting, especially when gathering for congregation in darkness or panic is dangerous.
The commentary highlights safety and order.
4
Distinguish the role of the imam
If an imam is present and can lead, congregation is preferred. The text implies the imam leads the prayer to maintain order.
This is supported by the Prophet's own practice during an eclipse.
5
Apply the ruling to similar cases
The ruling is not limited to eclipses; it extends to any terrifying natural phenomenon that could cause chaos during congregation.
The hadith cited encourages resorting to individual supplication and prayer.

Chapter of Istisqa (Prayer for Rain). (841) And if the imam is not present, they pray individually. (842) Like solar eclipse, terrifying darkness during daytime, strong wind, and panic. The commentary explains that when no imam is present, people would cause chaos, so if the imam is present he leads congregation; if not, they pray individually. For lunar eclipse, terrifying darkness, and wind, it is better to pray individually to avoid danger. Two hadith are cited: one from Muslim that the Prophet said to resort to remembrance, supplication, and seeking forgiveness during such signs; another from Bayhaqi that during dark winds, people would hasten to the mosque individually fearing the Day of Judgment. Vocabulary: انجلاء: clearing; الهائلة: terrifying; الفزع: panic.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement regarding prayer during natural calamities. It states that if the imam is not present, people should pray individually in cases of solar eclipse, lunar eclipse, terrifying daytime darkness, strong wind, and panic. The commentary explains that if an imam is present, he leads a congregational prayer; but if not, individual prayer is preferred to avoid chaos. For lunar eclipse (which occurs at night) and terrifying darkness, congregational prayer could lead to disorder, so it is better to pray alone. Two hadith are quoted: one from Muslim that during such signs, one should turn to remembrance, supplication, and seeking forgiveness; another from Bayhaqi that during severe wind, people would hasten to the mosque individually fearing the Last Day. This ruling is from the Hanafi school, emphasizing fear and individual devotion during unusual events.

Key Terms
الخسوف (al-khusuf): Lunar eclipse; the darkening of the moon.
الظلمة الهائلة (al-zulmat al-hā’ila): Terrifying or overwhelming darkness that occurs during daytime, often due to natural phenomena.
الفزع (al-faza‘): Panic or intense fear, here referring to a state of alarm that prompts prayer.

Ruling on Salat al-Istisqa: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on Istisqa prayer, including the dispute between Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding Salat al-Istisqa, identify their proofs, and explain the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Imam Abu Hanifa saw prayer for rain as optional; the Sahibayn made it a sunnah — the latter became the school's relied-upon view.

When drought strikes, Muslims turn to Allah for rain. But is a specific prayer required, or does supplication suffice? This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Understanding this difference clarifies the ruling on Salat al-Istisqa and the methodology of weighing proofs within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The central question: is Salat al-Istisqa obligatory (sunnah) or just permissible? Determine the exact point of disagreement.
Both agree the act is recommended; the dispute is whether a specific formal prayer is required.
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position and his evidence
Abu Hanifa holds that the prayer is not necessary; supplication and istighfar suffice. His proofs: Quran 71:10-11 (command to seek forgiveness) and hadith of Anas where the Prophet only supplicated.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their evidence
The Sahibayn hold that Salat al-Istisqa is sunnah. Their proof: hadith of 'Abbad ibn Tamim where the Prophet prayed two rak'ahs with loud recitation and turned his cloak.
4
Analyse the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Hanifa's view, one may simply make dua without formal prayer; under Sahibayn, a specific sunnah prayer is recommended with specific etiquettes.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi works adopt the Sahibayn's view; Salat al-Istisqa is sunnah muakkadah. Identify the tarjih authority.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب : استسقاء کے بیان میں
ضروری نوٹ : استقاء کے معنی ہیں بارش طلب کرنا ، یہ تھی سے مشتق ہے ، ملک میں قحط سالی ہو جائے اور بارش نہ ہو تو استسقاء کیا جاسکتا ہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک نماز پڑھنا کوئی ضروری نہیں ہے۔ صرف دعا سے بھی استسقاء ہو سکتا ہے اور نماز بھی

پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک نماز استسقاء مسنون ہے۔ دونوں کی دلیلیں نیچے آرہی ہیں۔ اس کی دلیل یہ آیت بھی ہے فقلت استغفروا ربكم انه كان غفارا يرسل السماء عليكم مدرارا o ) آیت ۱/۱۰ اسورۃ نوح ۱۷) اس آیت میں ہے کہ اپنے اپنے گناہوں سے تو بہ کرو تا کہ اللہ تعالی تم پر خوب بارش برسائے۔ اور چونکہ نماز استسقاء میں اپنے گناہوں سے تو بہ کرنا ہے اس لئے اس آیت سے استقاء ثابت ہوتا ہے۔
ترجمه : (۸۴۳) استقاء کی نماز ہے بغیر جماعت کے اور اس کے لئے استغفار ہے۔ تشریح : امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک جماعت کے ساتھ نماز استسقاء جائز ہے، البتہ بہتر یہ ہے کہ بغیر جماعت کے نماز استسقاء پڑھے اور دعا اور استغفار کرے، کیونکہ آیت میں استغفار کرنے کی ترغیب ہے۔
وجه: (1) اس آیت میں ہے کہ ۔ فقلت استغفروا ربكم انه كان غفارا يرسل السماء عليكم مدرارا o ( آیت، ارا اسورۃ نوح ۱۷) اس آیت میں ہے کہ بارش رک جائے تو استغفار کرو ۔ (۲) عن انس بن مالک ان رجلا دخل المسجـد يـوم الـجـمـعـة ورسول الله الا الله قائما يخطب ... فرفع رسول الله يديه قال اللهم اغثنا . ( بخاری شریف ، باب الاستسقاء في خطبة الجمعة غير مستقبل القبلة ، ص ۱۳۸، نمبر ۱۰۱۴ر مسلم شریف ، کتاب الاستسقاء ،ص۱۹۳، نمبر ۱۸۹۷ ۲۰۷۸ / ابوداؤد شریف، باب رفع الیدین فی الاستقاء، ص ۱۷۳، نمبر ۱۱۷۵ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ آپ نے اس کے لئے مستقل نماز نہیں پڑھی صرف دعا پر اکتفا کیا۔ اس لئے امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک نماز ضروری نہیں ،صرف دعا اور استغفار سے بھی استسقاء ہو جائے گا۔ اور نماز پڑھ لے تو کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے، کیونکہ وہ بھی حدیث سے ثابت ہے۔(۳) اگر نماز پڑھ لے اور جہری قرآت کرے تب بھی جائز ہے صاحبین کا یہ مسلک ہے ۔ اس کے لئے حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن عباد بن تميم عن عمه قال خرج النبي الله يستسقى فتوجه الى القبلة يدعو وحول رداء ٥ ثم صلى ركعتين يجهر فيهما بالقراء ة ـ ( بخاری شریف، باب الجهر بالقراءة فى الاستقاء ص ۱۳۹ نمبر ۱۰۲۴ر مسلم شریف ، کتاب صلوة الاستقاء، ص ۲۹۳، نمبر ۲۰۷۱/۸۹۴ ابوداؤد شریف، ابواب صلوۃ الاستسقاء، ص ۷۱ ا نمبر ۱۱۶۱) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ امام دورکعت نماز پڑھائیں گے۔ اور قرآت جہری کریں گے اور چادر کو بھی نیک فالی کے لئے پلٹیں گے کہ یا اللہ جس طرح چادر پلٹ رہا ہوں اس طرح میری حالت کو بھی پلیٹ دے۔ اور یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ دعا کے وقت قبلہ کی طرف استقبال کرے۔ ترجمه : (۸۴۴) اور اس کے لئے تین دن تک نکلنا مستحب ہے پیدل پرانے دھلے ہوئے، یا پیوند دار کپڑے میں ذلیل بن کر عاجزی کرتے ہوئے ، خدائے تعالی سے ڈرتے ہوئے سر جھکائے ہوئے۔
تشریح : اگر پہلے دن بارش نہ ہوتو بہتر ہے کہ تین دن تک نکلے، پیدل ہو، پرانا کپڑا دھلا ہوا ہو یا پیوند لگا ہوا ہو، ذلیل بن کر،
Chapter: Concerning Istisqa. Necessary Note: Istisqa means seeking rain, derived from 'saqa'. If a drought occurs and there is no rain, istisqa can be performed. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, praying is not necessary; istisqa can be done with supplication alone, but prayer is also allowed. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the prayer of istisqa is sunnah. Their proofs are given below. Among the proofs is this verse: 'Ask forgiveness of your Lord. Indeed, He is ever a Perpetual Forgiver. He will send [rain from] the sky upon you in [continuing] showers.' (Surah Nuh, 71:10-11). This verse indicates that if rain stops, one should seek forgiveness. Translation: (843) There is a prayer [for rain] without congregation, and there is seeking forgiveness for it. Commentary: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, praying istisqa in congregation is permissible, but it is better to pray without congregation and to make supplication and seek forgiveness, because the verse encourages seeking forgiveness. Proof (1): This verse. Proof (2): Hadith of Anas ibn Malik that a man entered the mosque on Friday while the Prophet was delivering the sermon... the Prophet raised his hands and said 'O Allah, give us rain.' (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud). This hadith shows that the Prophet did not perform a separate prayer but sufficed with supplication. Therefore, according to Abu Hanifa, prayer is not necessary; supplication and seeking forgiveness suffice. If one prays, there is no harm, as that is also established from hadith. (3) If one prays and recites aloud, it is permissible. This is the position of the Sahibayn, and the proof is the hadith of 'Abbad ibn Tamim from his uncle: 'The Prophet went out to seek rain, turned towards the qibla, made supplication, turned his cloak, then prayed two rak'ahs reciting aloud.' (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud). This shows that the imam leads two rak'ahs with loud recitation, turns his cloak for good omen, and faces the qibla during supplication. Translation: (844) It is recommended to go out for three days, walking, in old washed or patched clothes, humbly, in submission, fearing Allah, with heads bowed. Commentary: If rain does not come on the first day, it is better to go out for three days, walking, wearing old washed or patched clothes, humbly.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling on Salat al-Istisqa (prayer for rain) with an intra-Hanafi dispute. It begins by defining istisqa as seeking rain, and states that Imam Abu Hanifa considers the prayer itself not obligatory; one may simply supplicate and seek forgiveness, citing the Quranic verse (71:10-11) where Prophet Nuh commanded seeking forgiveness for rain. A hadith from Anas shows the Prophet only made supplication during Friday sermon, not a separate prayer. However, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that Salat al-Istisqa is sunnah, based on another hadith where the Prophet prayed two rak'ahs with loud recitation and turned his cloak. The text reconciles by saying both are permissible. It then translates ruling (843): there is a prayer without congregation, and seeking forgiveness. The preferred view of Abu Hanifa is to pray individually and make supplication, but if one prays in congregation or with loud recitation, it is also valid (position of Sahibayn). The text also mentions recommended etiquettes: going out for three days, walking, wearing humble clothes (old, washed, patched), with humility and fear of Allah. The commentary emphasizes turning the cloak as a symbol of hope for change. Overall, this passage provides the mas'ala with its proofs and the difference between Abu Hanifa and his disciples, without explicitly stating which is mufta bihi, though later Hanafi practice follows the Sahibayn that it is sunnah.

Key Terms
استسقاء (istisqā’): The act of seeking rain from Allah, typically through prayer and supplication during drought.
صلاة الاستسقاء (ṣalāt al-istisqā’): The specific prayer for rain, considered sunnah by Sahibayn.
صاحبين (ṣāḥibayn): The two students of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the key difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding Salat al-Istisqa?
A) Abu Hanifa says it is haram; Sahibayn say it is sunnah.
B) Abu Hanifa says it is not necessary; Sahibayn say it is sunnah.
C) Abu Hanifa says it is wajib; Sahibayn say it is makruh.
D) Both agree it is fard.

Key Takeaway
Salat al-Istisqa is a sunnah muakkadah in the Hanafi school (Sahibayn's view), performed in two rak'ahs with loud recitation, supplication, and cloak turning, though Imam Abu Hanifa considered it permissible without a formal prayer.

Recommended Practices for Istisqa': Humility and Charity
States the recommended practices for the prayer for rain, Part 1

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended practices for salat al-istisqa' according to the Hanafi school and cite the supporting hadith evidence from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
For istisqa', the Prophet's practice was humility, worn clothes, charity, and supplication—not a long sermon.

In times of drought, the Hanafi school prescribes salat al-istisqa' as a sunnah mu'akkadah. This lesson focuses on the recommended etiquettes (mustahabbat) to accompany the prayer: wearing humble clothes, displaying humility, giving charity beforehand, and focusing on supplication. These practices are rooted in the Prophet's example, as documented in the hadith cited by the author. You will learn the specific rulings and their evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended acts
From the text, list the specific actions described as recommended: wearing worn or patched clothes, showing humility, lowering heads, giving charity before going out, and including the elderly and helpless in a humble state.
2
Understand the ruling level
The text uses 'يستحب' (it is recommended), which in Hanafi fiqh corresponds to mustahabb. These actions are not obligatory but are meritorious.
Mustahabb is a category between sunnah and mubah in Hanafi terminology.
3
Locate the hadith proofs
The author cites three hadith: the Ibn Abbas hadith on the Prophet's practice, the Ibn Buraidah hadith linking charity with rain, and the Aisha hadith on charity during eclipses. Identify each.
These are ahad hadith, thus zanni in transmission.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
For the clothing and humility, the hadith directly describes the Prophet's actions (mubtadhalan, mutawadi'an). For charity, the connection is through the general cause of drought and the act of giving.
The Hanafi principle: al-amr bi al-shay' yufidu al-nadb when context indicates recommendation.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The Hanafi position is mustahabb, while some other schools may consider these sunnah mu'akkadah. The practical difference is minimal: both encourage the acts, but the precise fiqh classification affects emphasis.
The ayah 'ad' that is a subtle point of mujtahid reasoning.

باب الاستسقاء
ثياب خلقة غسيلة او مرقعة متذللين متواضعين خاشعين لله تعالى ناکسین رؤوسهم (۸۴۵) مـقـدميـن الصدقة كل يوم قبل خروجهم (۸۴۶) ويستحبّ اخراج الدواب والشيوخ الكبار عاجزی کرتے ہوئے ، اپنے سروں کو جھکائے ہوئے ، اور اس حال میں نماز پڑھے اور رو رو کر اللہ تعالی سے استغفار کرے اور بارش کے لئے دعائیں کرے۔
وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے ۔ ارسلنی الی ابن عباس أسأله عن صلاة رسول الله عله في الاستسقاء فقال صلى الله خرج رسول الله عالم مبتذلا متواضعا متضرعا حتى اتى المصلى ـ زاد عثمان فرقى على المنبر ثم اتفقا۔ فلم يخطب خطبكم هذه و لكن لم يزل في الدعاء و التضرع و التكبير ، ثم صلى ركعتين كما يصلي في العيد ۔ (ابوداود شریف، باب جماع ابواب صلاة الاستسقاء و تفریعھا، ص۱۷۴ نمبر ۱۶۵ ارترندی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی صلاۃ الاستسقاء، ص ۱۴۶ نمبر ۵۵۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور نیچے درجے کے کپڑے میں تواضع کے ساتھ روتے ہوئے باہر نکلے۔ ترجمه : (۸۴۵) اور ہر روز اپنے نکلنے سے پہلے صدقہ دیتے جائیں۔
وجه : عن ابن بريدة عن ابيه قال قال النبى الا الله ما نقض قوم العهد قط الا كان القتل بينهم و ما ظهرت فاحشة في قوم قط الا سلط الله عز و جل عليهم الموت ، و لا منع قوم الزكوة الا حبس ) الله عنهم القطر - ( سنن بیہقی ، باب الخروج من المظالم والتقرب الی اللہ تعالى بالصدقة و نوافل الخير رجاء الاجابة ، ج ثالث ،ص۴۸۲، نمبر ۶۳۹۷) اس حدیث میں زکوہ دینے اور صدقہ دینے کی طرف اشارہ ہے۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے۔ عن عائشة انها قالت خسفت الشمس في عهد رسول الله علل ..... فاذا رأيتم ذالك فاذكروا الله و كبروا وصلوا و تصدقوا ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب الصدقۃ فی الکسوف ، ص ۱۶۷، نمبر ۱۰۴۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ اس قسم کے حالات ہوں تو صدقہ کرو۔
Chapter of Istisqa. Worn, washed or patched clothes, humbling themselves, humble, submissive to Allah, lowering their heads (845), giving charity every day before their departure (846). It is recommended to take out animals, elderly great ones, helpless people, lowering their heads, and in that state they pray and seek forgiveness from Allah while weeping and make supplications for rain. Proof (1): In this hadith: He sent me to Ibn Abbas to ask him about the prayer of the Messenger of Allah for rain, and he said: The Messenger of Allah went out humble, wearing worn clothes, beseeching until he came to the prayer place – Uthman added: then he ascended the pulpit – then they agreed: He did not deliver the sermon like your sermon, but he continued in supplication, beseeching, and takbir, then he prayed two rak'ahs as he prays on the Eid. (Abu Dawud, Bab Jama' Abwab Salat al-Istisqa', p.174 no.165; Tirmidhi, Bab Ma Ja'a fi Salat al-Istisqa', p.146 no.558). In this hadith, the Prophet went out wearing low-grade clothes with humility, weeping. Translation (845): And every day before his departure, he gave charity. Proof: From Ibn Buraidah from his father, he said: The Prophet said: 'Indeed, no people ever broke a covenant except that killing was placed among them, and no immorality ever appeared among a people except that Allah Almighty inflicted death upon them, and no people ever withheld zakat except that Allah withheld rain from them.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-Khuruj min al-Mazalim wa al-Taqarrub ila Allah ta'ala bi al-Sadaqah wa Nawafil al-Khair, vol.3, p.482, no.6397). This hadith indicates giving zakat and charity. (2) Also in this hadith: From Aisha that she said: The sun eclipsed in the time of the Messenger of Allah... So if you see that, remember Allah, exalt Him, pray, and give charity. (Bukhari, Bab al-Sadaqah fi al-Kusuf, p.167, no.1044). In this hadith, when such situations occur, give charity.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage from Thamaratun Najah discusses the recommended practices (mustahabbat) for the salat al-istisqa' (prayer for rain). It is a ruling-with-proof passage: the author first states the rulings concisely, then provides supporting hadith evidence. The rulings cover two main points: (1) wearing humble, old, or patched clothes, displaying humility, lowering the head, and being submissive before Allah; (2) giving charity each day before going out for the prayer. The proofs include the famous hadith of Ibn Abbas describing the Prophet's practice: he went out wearing humble clothes, beseeching, and did not deliver a long sermon but focused on supplication, then prayed two rak'ahs like the Eid prayer. The second proof for charity is from Ibn Buraidah's hadith linking withholding zakat/charity to drought, and a third from Aisha connecting eclipse prayers with charity. In the Hanafi school, these actions are mustahabb (recommended), not wajib. They reflect the spirit of humility and seeking Allah's mercy during drought.

Key Terms
الاستسقاء (al-istisqā’): The prayer for rain, performed in times of drought.
متواضعین (mutawāḍi‘īn): Humbling oneself, displaying humility before Allah.
مبتذلا (mubtadhalan): Wearing humble, old, or worn clothes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Wajib
C) Mustahabb
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends humility, worn clothes, and charity before istisqa', based on the Prophet's example, to foster a sincere plea for rain.

Bringing the Weak to Istisqa': A Recommended Practice
Continues recommended practices for istisqa'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bringing the weak to istisqa' and identify the hadith proofs that support this recommendation.

Core Idea
Bringing the weak to istisqa' is mustahabb because their supplications draw Allah's mercy.

Istisqa' is a communal prayer for rain, and its effectiveness is enhanced by the presence of those most likely to invoke Allah's mercy. This lesson examines the Hanafi recommendation to include vulnerable beings—elderly, children, and animals—in the congregation, citing prophetic hadith that highlight the spiritual power of the weak.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Recommended Act
Locate in the text the specific actions recommended: taking out livestock, weak elderly, and children to the place of istisqa'.
The Urdu term 'مستحب' directly indicates the ruling level.
2
State the Ruling
The ruling is mustahabb (recommended). Explain that this is not obligatory but encouraged to increase the chance of the prayer being answered.
Mustahabb acts are rewarded when done, but not punished when omitted.
3
Locate the Dalil
The text provides two hadith from Sunan al-Bayhaqi. Identify them and note their key phrases.
Both are ahad hadith, giving zanni proof.
4
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
Explain how each hadith supports the ruling: the first links Allah's support of the ummah to the weak, implying their presence brings divine mercy; the second warns that without them, punishment would descend.
The second hadith lists 'shuyukh rukka' (bowing elders) and 'atfal ruda' (suckling infants) as among those whose absence would invite wrath.
5
Note the Practical Implication
Organizers of istisqa' should actively include and encourage participation of the vulnerable, not exclude them.
This ruling counteracts any tendency to think only strong, pious adults should attend.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۸۴۶) اور مستحب ہے چوپایوں کو نکالنا، کمزور بوڑھوں کو نکالنا، اور بچوں کو نکالنا۔ تشریح : یہ لوگ روئیں گے تو اللہ تعالی کو زیادہ رحم آئے گا ، اس لئے ان لوگوں کو ساتھ لے چلنا مستحب ہے۔

صل الله
الخروج بالضعفاء، والصبيان والعبيد والعجائز ، ج ثالث ص ۴۸۰، نمبر ۶۳۸۹) (۲) عن ابـي هــريـــة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال مهلا عـن الـلـه مهلا فانه لولا شباب خشع و بهائم رتع و شیوخ رکع و اطفال رضع لصب عليكم العذاب صبا. (سنن بیہقی ، باب استحباب الخروج بالضعفاء، والصبيان والعبيد والعجائز ، ج ثالث ،ص۴۸۰، نمبر ۶۳۸۹) ان احادیث میں ہے کہ کمزوروں سے روزی ملتی ہے اس لئے کمز ور لوگوں کو میدان میں لیجائے ۔
Translation (846): And it is recommended to take out livestock, weak elderly, and children. Explanation: These people will weep, so Allah Most High will have more mercy; therefore, taking these people along is recommended. (1) Mus'ab ibn Sa'd from his father: He thought he had superiority over those below him among the Companions of the Prophet, so the Prophet of Allah said: 'Allah Almighty only supports this ummah through its weak ones: by their supplication, prayer, and sincerity.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab Istihbab al-Khuruj bi al-Du'afa', wa al-Sibyan wa al-Abid wa al-Aja'iz, vol. 3, p. 480, no. 6389) (2) From Abu Hurairah from the Prophet: 'Slowly, concerning Allah, slowly. For if there were not humble youth, grazing beasts, bowing elders, and suckling infants, He would have poured down punishment upon you.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab Istihbab al-Khuruj bi al-Du'afa', wa al-Sibyan wa al-Abid wa al-Aja'iz, vol. 3, p. 480, no. 6389) In these hadiths, sustenance comes through the weak, so take weak people to the field.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage presents the second recommended practice for istisqa': bringing along livestock, elderly people, and children. The author explains that their weeping moves Allah's mercy more than that of others. Two hadith proofs are provided: one from Mus'ab ibn Sa'd where the Prophet states that Allah supports the ummah through its weak ones, highlighting the value of their supplications. The second from Abu Hurairah warns that without humble youth, grazing beasts, bowing elders, and suckling infants, punishment would descend. In the Hanafi school, this is a mustahabb (recommended) practice to increase the likelihood of the prayer being answered.

Key Terms
ضعفاء (ḍu‘afā’): Weak ones, including elderly, children, and animals.
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended; an action that is rewarded when done but not punished when omitted.
استسقاء (istisqā’): The prayer for rain during drought.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, it is mustahabb to bring livestock, elderly, and children to istisqa' because their sincere supplication attracts Allah's mercy.

Istisqa in Sacred Mosques: Makkah, Madinah, and Bayt al-Maqdis
Specifies the venue for istisqa in holy cities: inside the sacred mosques

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended venue for istisqa for residents of Makkah, Madinah, and Jerusalem, and explain why the Hanafi school prefers the mosque over the field in these cities.

Core Idea
Istisqa in holy cities is best performed inside the sacred mosques, not in the open field.

You already know that the general practice for istisqa is to go to an open field. This lesson presents a special exception for the three holiest cities: Makkah, Madinah, and Jerusalem. The Hanafi school teaches that the residents of these cities should instead gather in their respective sacred mosques due to the heightened acceptance of supplication there.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule and its exception
Recall that the default Hanafi position for istisqa is to go to an open field (musalla). This passage introduces an exception for residents of holy cities. Note the three cities and their corresponding mosques.
Makkah → Masjid al-Haram; Madinah → Prophet's Mosque; Jerusalem → Masjid al-Aqsa.
2
State the Hanafi position for each city
The text uses terms like 'مناسب' (appropriate) and 'بہتر' (better), indicating recommendation (mustahabb). For Makkah and Jerusalem, it directly states to gather in the mosque; for Madinah, it says 'appropriate' in the Prophet's Mosque, with a note that the Prophet sometimes went outside.
The ruling is mustahabb, not wajib. The mosque is preferred but not obligatory.
3
Locate the dalil (proof)
The author cites the hadith of Anas ibn Malik where the Prophet made istisqa supplication while delivering a Friday sermon inside the mosque. This shows it is permissible and even preferred to pray for rain in a mosque.
Hadith from Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud. The operative phrase is 'فرفع رسول الله يديه قال اللهم اغثنا'.
4
Analyze the dalil's implication
The hadith proves that the Prophet performed istisqa inside the mosque, thus establishing its permissibility. The Hanafi school extends this into a preference for sacred mosques, where the virtue of place enhances acceptance.
The dalil is zanni in thubut and dalala, but sufficient for istihbab (recommendation).
5
Note the practical consequence
The exception applies only to these three cities. For all other places, the general rule of going to the field remains. Ignoring this exception for holy cities would mean missing a more meritorious practice.
The text also notes that the Prophet sometimes went outside Madinah, showing that the mosque is not obligatory.

Source Text

( بخاری شریف ، باب الاستسقاء في خطبة الجمعة غير مستقبل القبلة ، ص۱۶۳، نمبر ۱۰۱۴ر مسلم شریف ، کتاب الاستسقاء ص ۱۳۵۸، نمبر ۲۰۷۸/۸۹۷ را بو داؤد شریف، باب رفع الیدین فی الاستسقاء ، ص ۱۷۳، نمبر ۱۱۷۵)
Translation (847): And if it is Makkah, then in the Sacred Mosque, and if it is Bayt al-Maqdis, then in al-Aqsa Mosque, they gather. And for the people of the city of the Prophet, it is appropriate in the Prophet's Mosque. Explanation: It came earlier that for the istisqa prayer, one goes to the field so that the supplication is accepted. But for the people of Makkah, they should pray in the House of Allah, because this sacred place is very suitable for the acceptance of supplication. Similarly, the people of Bayt al-Maqdis gather in al-Aqsa Mosque, and it is better that the people of Madinah gather in the Prophet's Mosque to make supplications, because supplications in this sacred mosque are very appropriate for acceptance. However, the Prophet sometimes went outside Madinah for istisqa. Proof (2): For supplication in the Prophet's Mosque for istisqa, there is this hadith: Anas ibn Malik: A man entered the mosque on Friday while the Messenger of Allah was standing giving the sermon... So the Messenger of Allah raised his hands and said: 'O Allah, send us rain! O Allah, send us rain! O Allah, send us rain!' (Bukhari, Bab al-Istisqa fi Khutbat al-Jumu'ah ghayr Mustaqbil al-Qiblah, p.163, no.1014; Muslim, Kitab al-Istisqa, p.1358, no.2078/897; Abu Dawud, Bab Raf' al-Yadayn fi al-Istisqa, p.173, no.1175)

Commentary
This passage addresses an exception to the general rule of going to the open field for istisqa. For the residents of Makkah, Madinah, and Jerusalem, the preferred venue is the respective sacred mosque: Masjid al-Haram, the Prophet's Mosque, and Masjid al-Aqsa. The author explains that these holy places are more suitable for acceptance of supplication. However, he notes that the Prophet sometimes went outside Madinah for istisqa, indicating that the mosque is not obligatory but recommended. The proof provided is the hadith of Anas where the Prophet raised his hands in the mosque during Friday sermon and prayed for rain, showing that istisqa supplication can be made inside a mosque. In the Hanafi school, while going to a public place (musalla) is generally preferred, doing it in these sacred mosques is even better due to the sanctity of the location.

Key Terms
مسجد حرام (Masjid al-Ḥarām): The Sacred Mosque in Makkah, the holiest site in Islam.
استسقاء (istisqāʾ): The ritual prayer for rain, consisting of a congregational prayer and supplication.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) In the Prophet's Mosque
C) In any local mosque
D) On a mountain

Key Takeaway
For the holy cities of Makkah, Madinah, and Jerusalem, the Hanafi school recommends performing istisqa in the sacred mosques, not in the open field.

Posture of Imam and Congregation in Istisqa Supplication
Describes the recommended posture for istisqa: imam facing qibla, raising hands

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the posture of the imam and congregation during istisqa supplication, identify the proofs from the Sunnah, and distinguish the Hanafi position from other schools.

Core Idea
In istisqa, the imam stands facing qibla with raised hands; the congregation sits and says amin.

This lesson examines the recommended posture during the special supplication for rain (istisqa). While the imam stands and raises his hands high, the Hanafi school teaches that the congregation should sit facing the qibla and respond with amin. We will explore the proof from the Prophet's practice and the wisdom behind the difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the istisqa supplication (not the full prayer). The ruling is sunnah muakkadah (emphasised sunnah).
The text clearly describes the Prophet's practice as recommended.
2
Locate the dalil
Three hadiths are cited: (1) 'Ubad ibn Tamim's uncle reports the Prophet stood, faced qibla, and supplicated. (2) Anas reports the Prophet raised his hands high in istisqa. (3) Another hadith shows the Prophet and people raising hands together.
All are from Bukhari and Muslim, thus sound (sahih).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit actions (standing, facing qibla, raising hands) indicate the recommended form. The hadith do not specify the congregation's posture, so Hanafis derive the ruling from other principles (e.g., avoiding resemblance to the imam's standing).
The Hanafi deduction is based on the general practice of the Companions.
4
Note the Hanafi distinctive ruling
The Hanafi school holds that the congregation sits facing qibla and says amin, while only the imam stands. This is based on the practice of the early Muslims and to distinguish the supplication from the prayer.
This is a sunnah muakkadah; its omission is not sinful but losing a reward.
5
Consider cross‑madhhab difference
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) have the congregation stand and raise hands like the imam. The Hanafi position is the mufta bihi in the school.
Both positions are legitimate, based on different understandings of the same hadith.

Translation (848): And the imam stands facing the qibla, raising both his hands, and the people face the qibla, sitting, and say amin to his supplication. Explanation: When making supplication, observe these matters: the imam faces qibla standing, both hands raised; the followers also face qibla but sitting, and say amin to the imam's supplication. In istisqa, he raised his hands so high that he did not raise them so much in any other prayer. Proof: (1) 'Ubad ibn Tamim narrated that his uncle, who was among the Companions of the Prophet, told him that the Prophet went out with the people to pray for rain; he stood, supplicated to Allah standing, then turned towards the qibla, turned his cloak, and they were given rain. (Bukhari, Bab al-Du'a' fi al-Istisqa Qa'iman, p.125, no.1023; Muslim, Kitab Salat al-Istisqa, p.1358, no.2073/894) In this hadith, the Prophet stood, faced the qibla, and supplicated. (2) From Anas: The Prophet would not raise his hands in any supplication except in istisqa, until the whiteness of his armpits was seen. (Muslim, Bab Raf' al-Yadayn bi al-Du'a' fi al-Istisqa, p.1359, no.2076/896) This hadith shows that he raised his hands very high. (3) I heard Anas ibn Malik: A Bedouin man came to the Messenger of Allah on Friday and said: 'O Messenger of Allah, the livestock have perished, the families have perished, the people have perished.' So the Messenger of Allah raised his hands in supplication, and the people raised their hands with him, supplicating. (Bukhari)
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage provides the specific recommended posture during the istisqa supplication. The imam stands facing the qibla with both hands raised high, while the congregation sits facing the qibla and responds with amin. Three hadiths are cited as proof: (1) The hadith of 'Ubad ibn Tamim's uncle shows the Prophet stood, faced qibla, and made supplication. (2) The hadith of Anas emphasizes raising hands high, to the point of seeing armpits. (3) Another hadith of Anas shows the Prophet and people raising hands together. In the Hanafi school, the imam stands; the congregation sits, which is a distinctive posture. The raising of hands high is a sunnah specific to istisqa.

Key Terms
قائما (qā’iman): Standing, the posture of the imam during istisqa supplication.
استسقاء (istisqā’): Supplication for rain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Sitting facing the qibla and saying amin
C) Prostrating

Key Takeaway
The imam stands, raises hands high, and faces qibla; congregation sits, faces qibla, and says amin.

Where to Perform Istisqa: Sacred Mosques Preferred
Ruling on where to pray for rain in holy cities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the recommended location for istisqa prayer in the three sacred cities and apply the hadith proof.

Core Idea
For Makkah, Madinah, and Bayt al-Maqdis, istisqa in the holiest mosque is better than an open field.

While the general practice for istisqa (rain prayer) is to go out to an open field to show humility and seek acceptance, the Hanafi school makes an exception for the three sacred cities: Makkah, Madinah, and Bayt al-Maqdis. This lesson examines the ruling, its basis in a prophetic hadith, and the reasoning behind prioritizing the sacred mosques.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
Recall that the sunnah for istisqa is to go to an open field (musalla) outside the town. This is the default Hanafi position.
The source mentions this as the background before introducing the exception.
2
State the exception for sacred cities
For Makkah, the people gather in Masjid al-Haram; for Bayt al-Maqdis, in Masjid al-Aqsa; and for Madinah, it is recommended to gather in the Prophet's Mosque.
The source uses 'yanbaghi' (recommended) for Madinah, indicating it is a strong recommendation.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
The proof is the hadith of Anas ibn Malik: the Prophet (peace be upon him) made istisqa supplication while delivering the Friday sermon inside the mosque, not in the field.
The hadith shows that praying in the mosque for rain is established by the Sunnah, especially in the Prophet's Mosque.
4
Understand the reasoning
The sacredness of these mosques makes them more suitable for supplication. The source states that supplication in these places is more likely to be accepted.
This is based on the virtue of these locations, not a strict legal obligation.
5
Apply the ruling
When asked about istisqa in Makkah, Madinah, or Bayt al-Maqdis, advise performing it in the respective sacred mosque. For other cities, follow the general rule of going to the field.
Note that the Prophet also went to the field on some occasions, so this is a preference, not an absolute rule.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on where to perform the istisqa prayer for residents of Makkah, Bayt al-Maqdis, and Madinah. The author states that while normally istisqa is performed in an open field, for these three sacred cities it is better to perform it in their respective holiest mosques: Masjid al-Haram for Makkah, Masjid al-Aqsa for Bayt al-Maqdis, and the Prophet's Mosque for Madinah. The reason given is that these mosques are especially conducive to the acceptance of supplication. The proof is a hadith of Anas ibn Malik (may Allah be pleased with him) showing the Prophet (peace be upon him) making istisqa in the mosque during the Friday sermon. The ruling is a recommendation (yambaghi/yanbaghi), not an obligation.

Key Terms
استسقاء (istisqa): The prayer and supplication for rain during drought.
مسجد الحرام (Masjid al-Haram): The Sacred Mosque in Makkah, the holiest site in Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The Prophet's Mosque
C) Any mosque in the city
D) The outskirts of the city

Key Takeaway
For the three sacred cities, performing istisqa in their holiest mosque is a recommended sunnah based on the Prophet's example in the hadith of Anas.

Sunnah Acts of Imam and Congregation in Istisqa Supplication
Ruling with proof on imam and congregation posture in istisqa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah acts of the imam and congregation during istisqa supplication and cite the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
The imam stands facing qibla with raised hands; the congregation sits and says amin — a sunnah established by Prophetic practice.

In this lesson, we examine the specific sunnah acts for the istisqa (prayer for rain) supplication. The Hanafi school derives these practices from explicit hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him). Understanding these details ensures that this communal supplication is performed in accordance with the sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the posture of the imam and congregation during the istisqa du'a. According to the Hanafi school, these actions are sunnah muakkadah (emphasized recommended).
Sunnah muakkadah means the Prophet regularly performed it; leaving it is disliked but not sinful.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites three hadith from Bukhari and Muslim. The primary narration is from Abbad ibn Tamim's uncle about the Prophet going out for istisqa, standing, facing qibla, and turning his cloak.
The second hadith from Anas emphasizes raising hands high; the third shows the congregation sitting and saying amin.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's actual practice (fi'l) demonstrates recommendation. The specificity of raising hands high only in istisqa shows it is a distinctive sunnah.
Fi'l of the Prophet indicates permissibility and, when done consistently, recommendation.
4
Note the congregational role
The hadith explicitly state: 'الناس قعود مستقبلين القبلة يؤمنون على دعائه' — the people sit facing qibla and say amin to his supplication. They do not raise hands high like the imam.
This distinguishes the imam's role from the congregation's.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, when performing istisqa, the imam should stand, face qibla, and raise his hands high; the congregation should sit facing qibla and say amin softly or quietly after each du'a.
If the congregation is large, they may sit on the ground or on prayer mats.

And the imam stands facing the qibla, raising (his hands). Translation: (848) The imam should stand facing the qibla with both hands raised, and the people should sit facing the qibla and say amin to his supplication. Explanation: During the supplication, these matters should be observed: the imam stands facing qibla with both hands raised, the followers also face qibla but while sitting, and they say amin to the imam's supplication. He used to raise his hands so high during istisqa that he did not raise them like that in any other situation. Evidence: (1) Hadith of Abbad ibn Tamim from his uncle... that the Prophet went out with the people for istisqa, stood, supplicated standing, then turned to the qibla and turned his cloak, and they were given rain. (Bukhari, Muslim). (2) Hadith of Anas that the Prophet used not to raise his hands in any supplication except istisqa, until the whiteness of his armpits was seen. (Muslim). (3) Hadith of Anas: a bedouin came to the Prophet on Friday and complained, so the Prophet raised his hands while supplicating, and the people raised their hands with him. (Bukhari) [Continuation on next page: And the people sit facing the qibla, saying amin to his supplication.]
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage gives the recommended posture for the imam and congregation during the istisqa supplication. The imam stands facing the qibla with hands raised high, while the congregation sits facing the qibla and says amin. The author emphasizes that the Prophet (peace be upon him) raised his hands higher in istisqa than in any other supplication. The proofs are three hadith: (1) the Prophet went out for istisqa and prayed while standing and facing qibla, and also turned his cloak; (2) he raised his hands so high that the whiteness of his armpits was visible; (3) he and the people raised their hands together. The last part on page 101 clarifies that the people sit facing qibla saying amin. This is the established sunnah.

Key Terms
استسقاء (istisqa): The act of praying for rain, typically performed as a special prayer and supplication during drought.
قبلة (qibla): The direction of the Kaaba in Makkah.
آمین (amin): A word said after supplication meaning 'O Allah, accept'.

The Prescribed Supplication for Istisqa
Ruling on the specific du'a to recite during istisqa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the du'a for istisqa, identify its proof from the hadith, and explain the flexibility in its recitation.

Core Idea
The prescribed du'a for istisqa is sunnah, confirmed by the Prophet's own supplication – flexibility in wording is allowed.

When seeking rain through the istisqa prayer, the imam leads the congregation in a specific supplication. This lesson examines the text of that du'a, its recommended status, and the prophetic proof that establishes it. You will learn not only the words but also the legal flexibility the Hanafi school permits.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the recitation of a specific du'a during the istisqa prayer. According to the Hanafi school, the ruling is sunnah muakkadah (emphatically recommended), not wajib.
This is a sunnah within a sunnah – the istisqa prayer itself is also sunnah muakkadah.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith narrated by Murrah ibn Ka'b in Sunan al-Bayhaqi, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) supplicated with the words 'Allahumma asqina...' after the people of Mudar were punished.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), which yields a recommendation, not obligation.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's own supplication establishes the precedent. The imperative 'asqina' (give us rain) is a request, not a command of obligation. Thus the du'a is prescribed as a sunnah.
The Hanafi principle: al-amr (command) indicates obligation unless there is a qarinah (indication) otherwise. Here, the context shows it is a du'a, not a legislative command.
4
Note the flexibility in recitation
The passage states 'this du'a or similar' (هذه الدعاء أو ما اشبهه), indicating that the exact wording is not mandatory. The imam may use similar words that convey the same meaning.
This flexibility applies to both the wording and the volume (softly or loudly).
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, the imam may choose to recite the transmitted du'a or any other supplication for rain, as long as the essence is maintained. The du'a may be recited softly or loudly.
The mufta bihi position: the imam can recite this or similar words, softly or loudly, without restriction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۸۴۹) امام یہ دعا یا اس کے مشابہ ہو آ ہستہ پڑھے یا زور سے پڑھے۔ دعا یہ ہے: اللهم اسقنا غيثاً مغيثاً هنيئاً مريئاً مريعاً غدقاً مجللاً سحاً طبقاً دائماً ۔ ترجمہ : اے اللہ ہمیں سیراب کر دے ایسی بارش سے جو سختی سے چھڑا دینے والی ہو، مبارک خوشگوار ہو ،شاداب کر دینے والی موسلا دھار ہو، چھا جانے والی تیز ، زمین کو گھیر نے والی متواتر ہو۔ وجه : اس حدیث میں اوپر کی دعا ہے۔ مرة بن كـعـب ــ حدثنا حديثا سمعته من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال سمعت رسول الله الله دعا على مضر فأتيته فقلت يا رسول الله ان الله قد اعطاک و استجاب لک و آن قومک قد هلكوا فادع الله لهم فقال (( اللهم اسقنا غيثا مغيثا مريا مريعا غدقا طبقا عاجلا غير رائث نافعا غير ضار )) فما كان الا جمعة او نحوها حتى سقوا ۔ (سنن بیہقی ، باب الدعا فی الاستقاء، ج ثالث ، ص ۴۹۶، نمبر ۶۴۴۰)
Translation: (849) The imam recites this supplication or similar, either softly or loudly. The supplication is: 'O Allah, grant us rain that brings relief, wholesome, pleasant, productive, abundant, covering, pouring, enveloping, continuous.' Explanation: 'O Allah, give us such rain that relieves hardship, blessed, enjoyable, refreshing, torrential, covering, swift, continuous.' Evidence: The above supplication is in this hadith: Murrah ibn Ka'b narrated a hadith he heard from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) that the Messenger of Allah supplicated against Mudar, so I came and said: 'O Messenger of Allah, Allah has given you and responded to you, and your people are perishing, so supplicate for them.' He said: 'O Allah, give us rain that brings relief, pleasant, productive, abundant, covering, swift, not delayed, beneficial, not harmful.' And within a week or so, they were given rain. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi)
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage provides the recommended supplication for the istisqa prayer. The imam may recite it either softly or loudly. The specific words are given in Arabic, asking Allah for a rain that is 'ghaythan mughithan' (relieving rain) with various positive attributes. The proof is a hadith from Murrah ibn Ka'b where the Prophet himself supplicated with similar words after the people of Mudar were punished. This du'a is thus a direct sunnah. The Hanafi position is that this du'a is prescribed and recommended.

Key Terms
غيث (ghayth): Rain that brings relief and benefit.
مغيث (mughith): That which delivers from hardship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It must be recited loudly only

Key Takeaway
The prescribed du'a for istisqa is a confirmed sunnah, with flexibility in wording and delivery.

Turning the Cloak in Istisqa: Permissible, Not Sunnah
Ruling that turning the cloak is not part of the sunnah of istisqa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school considers turning the cloak during istisqa as permissible (mubah) and not sunnah, and cite the hadith evidence used.

Core Idea
Not every action of the Prophet (PBUH) is a sunnah; some are merely permissible acts (mubah) that may be done or left.

This passage addresses a common misconception: because the Prophet turned his cloak during the istisqa supplication, many assume it is a recommended sunnah. The Hanafi school clarifies that while the action is permissible, it is not part of the prescribed sunnah of the istisqa prayer. By examining the hadith and the distinction between the Prophet's habitual actions and his emphasized practices, we learn an important principle of fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is turning the cloak (rida') during the istisqa prayer. The ruling is that it is not sunnah; it is merely permissible (ja'iz/mubah).
The text explicitly says 'sunnat nahin hai' (it is not sunnah).
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence is the hadith of Abbad ibn Tamim (Bukhari, Muslim) where the Prophet turned his cloak during istisqa.
The hadith is cited to show the action occurred, not to prove it is sunnah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith records the Prophet's action, but it does not contain a command or explicit recommendation to repeat it. Therefore, it is not elevated to sunnah status.
Hanafi usul: an action alone, without a command or consistent emphasis, does not create a sunnah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools may consider it sunnah because the Prophet did it consistently. The Hanafi response is that there is no command and the action is not part of the prescribed acts of istisqa.
The cross-madhhab status is 'mukhtalaf fih' (disputed).
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that turning the cloak is allowed but not a sunnah. It is neither recommended nor prohibited.
The authority weight is zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۸۵۰) اور اس میں چادر پھیرانا سنت نہیں ہے۔ تشریح : حدیث میں ہے کہ استقاء کی دعا مانگتے وقت حضور نے چادر پلٹی تھی کہ ائے اللہ میری حالت بھی اسی طرح پلیٹ دے، اس لئے چادر پلٹنا جائز تو ہے لیکن نماز استسقاء کی سنت میں سے نہیں ہے، چاہے تو کرے اور چاہے تو نہ کرے۔ وجه : (۱) حدثني عباد بن تميم ان عمه و كان من اصحاب النبي الله ، اخبره ان النبي عل خرج بالناس يستسقى لهم فقام فدعا الله قائما ثم توجه قبل القبلة و حول ردائه فاسقوا ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب الدعاء في الاستسقاء قائما ص ۱۶۵، نمبر ۱۰۲۳ر مسلم شریف ، کتاب صلوة الاستقاء ص ۳۵۸ نمبر ۲۰۷۳/۸۹۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور نے چادر لپٹی ہے۔
Translation: (850) Turning the cloak in it is not sunnah. Explanation: In the hadith, when asking for rain, the Prophet turned his cloak, as if to say 'O Allah, change my condition like this.' Therefore, turning the cloak is permissible but it is not from the sunnah of istisqa prayer; one may do it or not. Evidence: (1) Hadith of Abbad ibn Tamim that the Prophet went out with the people for istisqa, stood, supplicated, turned to the qibla, and turned his cloak, and they were given rain. (Bukhari, Muslim) In this hadith, the Prophet turned his cloak.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage clarifies an important point: although the Prophet (peace be upon him) turned his cloak during the istisqa supplication, this action is not considered a sunnah (established practice) of the prayer. Rather, it is merely permissible (ja'iz). The author explains that the turning of the cloak was symbolic, asking Allah to change their condition. The proof is the same hadith cited earlier, but the author distinguishes between what the Prophet did as a habitual action and what he emphasized as part of the sunnah. Therefore, while one may imitate this action, it is not a required or even recommended part of the istisqa prayer. The Hanafi view is that it is allowed but not a sunnah that brings extra reward.

Key Terms
رداء (rida'): The outer cloak or garment worn over the shoulders.
سنت (sunnah): A recommended practice that yields reward but is not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is a sunnah muakkadah
B) It is permissible but not sunnah
C) It is haram to turn the cloak
D) It is obligatory to turn it

Key Takeaway
Turning the cloak during istisqa is permissible but not a sunnah; it is not part of the prescribed acts of the prayer.

Dhimmis Should Not Attend Istisqa
Ruling with reason

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling regarding the presence of dhimmis in the istisqa prayer and explain the reason behind it.

Core Idea
It is better for dhimmis to stay away from istisqa because their presence may hinder the acceptance of supplication due to divine wrath.

This lesson addresses a specific ruling about who should be present during the istisqa (prayer for rain) gathering. The Hanafi school advises that non-Muslim subjects (dhimmis) should not attend, based on the belief that their presence might prevent the prayer from being accepted. Let's explore the reasoning and the precise legal status of this recommendation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What act is being ruled upon? (Attending istisqa). What is the ruling? (It is discouraged for dhimmis to attend).
The ruling is not a prohibition but a dislikedness.
2
Understand the reasoning
Why is it discouraged? Because the wrath of Allah descends upon dhimmis, possibly hindering the acceptance of the supplication.
The text mentions 'ghazab' (wrath) as the reason.
3
Classify the legal status
In Hanafi fiqh, this falls under makruh tanzih (slightly disliked). It is not haram.
Other schools may differ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۸۵۱) اور اس میں مشرکین حاضر نہ ہوں ۔ تشریح : استقاء میں ایسے لوگ حاضر ہوں جن سے دعا زیادہ قبول ہوتی ہے، اور ذمی پر اللہ کا غضب اترتا ہے اس لئے ان کو حاضر نہ کرے تو اچھا ہے۔
Translation: (851) And in it, polytheists should not be present. Explanation: In istisqa, those people from whom supplication is more accepted should be present, and the wrath of Allah descends upon the dhimmi, so it is good if they are not made present.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This final passage gives a ruling about who should attend the istisqa gathering. The author states that polytheists (mushrikun) should not be present. In the explanation, he specifies that this includes dhimmis (protected non-Muslim citizens). The reason given is that the supplication of believers is more accepted, and the presence of dhimmis may invite Allah's wrath, thus hindering the acceptance of the prayer. Therefore, it is recommended that only Muslims attend the istisqa gathering. This ruling is based on the idea that istisqa is a time of earnest supplication, and only those with strong faith should be present to maximize the chance of acceptance.

Key Terms
ذمی (dhimmi): A non-Muslim living under Islamic protection with a pact.
مشرکین (mushrikun): Those who associate partners with Allah; here used broadly to include non-Muslims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
