A) They do not believe in Allah
B) The wrath of Allah descends upon them
C) They are not allowed in mosques
D) They might disrupt the prayer

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling is that it is better for dhimmis not to attend istisqa due to the possibility of hindering the prayer's acceptance, but it is not prohibited.

Rulings on the Prayer for Rain (Istisqa)
Chapter on istisqa with rulings on dua, hand-raising, cloak, and dhimmi attendance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the prayer for rain, including the supplication, hand-raising, turning of the cloak, and attendance of non-Muslims, and identify the proof for each.

Core Idea
Istisqa is a confirmed sunnah; turning the cloak is permissible but not a sunnah, and non-Muslims should not attend.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah lays out the key rulings for the prayer for rain (istisqa). It covers the manner of supplication, the position of the congregation, the controversial act of turning the cloak, and who should be present. Understanding these details ensures the prayer is performed in accordance with the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the prayer for rain (istisqa). According to the Hanafi school, it is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah). Note the imam's role: he raises his hands, and the congregation sits facing the qibla, saying 'ameen'.
2
Locate the dalil
The passage cites a hadith for turning the cloak (from Bukhari/Muslim) and implies other proofs for the dua. The primary dalil is the practice of the Prophet (ﷺ) who performed istisqa with supplication.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith shows the Prophet turned his cloak, but the author interprets this as permissible, not sunnah. The Hanafi position is that the Prophet’s action was a specific occasion (not a general sunnah).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars (e.g., Shafi'is) consider turning the cloak part of the sunnah. The Hanafi school disagrees, as stated in the passage: 'ليس في قلب رداء'.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that turning the cloak is permissible but not sunnah. The ruling on non-Muslims (dhimmis) not attending is based on seeking acceptance of dua.

صلى الله
)) فما كان الا جمعة او نحوها حتى سقوا ۔ (سنن بیہقی ، باب الدعا فی الاستقاء، ج ثالث ، ص ۴۹۶، نمبر ۶۴۴۰)۔ ترجمه : (۸۵۰) اور اس میں چادر پھیرانا سنت نہیں ہے۔ تشریح : حدیث میں ہے کہ استقاء کی دعا مانگتے وقت حضور نے چادر پلٹی تھی کہ ائے اللہ میری حالت بھی اسی طرح پلیٹ دے، اس لئے چادر پلٹنا جائز تو ہے لیکن نماز استسقاء کی سنت میں سے نہیں ہے، چاہے تو کرے اور چاہے تو نہ کرے۔ وجه : (۱) حدثني عباد بن تميم ان عمه و كان من اصحاب النبي الله ، اخبره ان النبي عل خرج بالناس يستسقى لهم فقام فدعا الله قائما ثم توجه قبل القبلة و حول ردائه فاسقوا ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب الدعاء في الاستسقاء قائما ص ۱۶۵، نمبر ۱۰۲۳ر مسلم شریف ، کتاب صلوة الاستقاء ص ۳۵۸ نمبر ۲۰۷۳/۸۹۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور نے چادر لپٹی ہے۔ ترجمه : (۸۵۱) اور اس میں مشرکین حاضر نہ ہوں ۔ تشریح : استقاء میں ایسے لوگ حاضر ہوں جن سے دعا زیادہ قبول ہوتی ہے، اور ذمی پر اللہ کا غضب اترتا ہے اس لئے ان کو
حاضر نہ کرے تو اچھا ہے۔
Chapter of Istisqa. (The imam raises his hands, and the people sit, facing the qibla, saying 'ameen' to his supplication) (849) He says: 'O Allah, give us rain that is bringing relief, pleasant, wholesome, causing vegetation, abundant, covering, torrential, widespread, continuous' or similar, quietly or loudly. (850) And there is no turning of the cloak. (851) And no dhimmi should be present. [Urdu commentary explains: (849) The imam recites this dua or similar quietly or loudly. The dua is: 'Allahumma asqina ghaythan mughithan...' (850) Turning the cloak is not sunnah; it is permitted but not part of the sunnah of the prayer for rain. (851) Non-Muslims should not be present because their presence invites wrath.]
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage from Thamaratun Najah presents the rulings for the prayer for rain (salat al-istisqa). The imam leads the people, raising his hands in supplication while the congregation says 'ameen'. The recommended supplication is given: 'Allahumma asqina ghaythan mughithan...' (O Allah, give us a beneficial rain). The imam may recite it aloud or silently. A key point is that turning the cloak (qalb al-rida') is not a sunnah of this prayer, though it is permissible based on the Prophet's action. The author clarifies it is not part of the established sunnah. Additionally, non-Muslims (dhimmis) should not attend, as their presence is disliked; only those whose prayers are more accepted should be present.

Key Terms
استسقاء (istisqa): The prayer for rain, a confirmed sunnah performed when there is drought.
قلب رداء (qalb al-rida'): Turning the cloak or garment as an act during the prayer for rain.
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim subject living under Muslim rule with a covenant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on turning the cloak (qalb al-rida') during the prayer for rain (istisqa)?
A) It is a sunnah muakkadah.
B) It is permissible but not part of the sunnah.
C) It is makruh.
D) It is obligatory.

Key Takeaway
Istisqa is a confirmed sunnah; the key rulings are raising hands, facing qibla, saying ameen, and avoiding turning the cloak as a sunnah and excluding non-Muslims from attendance.

Permissibility of Salat al-Khawf
States the ruling and proofs for Salat al-Khawf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Salat al-Khawf, identify its conditions, and cite the Quranic and hadith proofs.

Core Idea
Salat al-Khawf is a concession for extreme fear, not limited to battle.

This lesson examines the permissibility of the fear prayer (Salat al-Khawf), a concession granted in situations of overwhelming danger. The Hanafi school, based on Quran and Sunnah, allows this prayer not only in the presence of an enemy but also when fearing drowning or fire. We will explore the textual proofs and the specific conditions that trigger this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules that Salat al-Khawf is jāʾiz (permissible). Note that it is a rukhsa (concession), not an obligatory form of prayer.
Jāʾiz here means permissible with conditions.
2
List the conditions for permissibility
The text states it is permissible in the presence of an enemy (bi-ḥuḍūri ʿadū) or with fear of drowning or burning (bi-khawfi ghariq aw ḥariq).
The Hanafi school extends this to other life-threatening dangers by qiyas.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
The passage cites Surah an-Nisa 4:102, which describes the method of prayer during battle. The imperative 'faqim' (so stand) indicates permission, and the detailed description shows the manner.
The verse is qaṭʿī al-thubūt but ẓannī al-dalāla for the exact ruling.
4
Examine the hadith proof
The hadith of ʿAbdullāh ibn ʿUmar narrates the Prophet ṣallallāhu ʿalayhi wa sallam leading the prayer in ranks during an expedition to Najd.
This hadith demonstrates the practice and confirms the method.
5
Note the Hanafi extension
Unlike some schools that restrict Salat al-Khawf to enemy presence, the Hanafi school includes other dangers by analogy (qiyas) from the underlying cause of fear.
The extension is based on the broader ʿilla of extreme fear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلوة الخوف (۸۵۲) هي جائزة بحضور عدو وبخوف غرق او حرق

وجه : (۱) واذا كنت فيهم فاقمت لهم الصلوة فلتقم طائفة منهم معك وليأخذوا اسلحتهم فاذا سجدوا فليكونوا من ورائكم ولتأت طائفة اخرى لم يصلوا فليصلوا معك وليأخذوا حذرهم واسلحتهم ود الذين كفروا لو تغفلون عن اسلحتكم و أمتعتكم فيميلون عليكم ميلة واحدة - ( آیت ۱۰۲،سورۃ النساء۴ ) اس آیت سے ثابت ہوا کہ نماز خوف پڑھ سکتا ہے، اور یہ بھی پتہ چلا کہ کس طرح پڑھے۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے ۔ ان عبد الله بن عمر قال غزوت مع رسول الله الله قبل نجد فوازينا العدو فصاففنا لهم فقام رسول الله يصلى لنا فقامت طائفة معه و اقبلت طائفة على العدو وفركع رسول الله الا الله بمن معه و سجد سجدتين ثم انصرفوا
Chapter of Salat al-Khawf. (852) It is permissible in the presence of an enemy and with fear of drowning or burning. Evidence: (1) 'And when you are among them, you stand for prayer, then let a party of them stand with you and let them take their arms; then when they prostrate, let them be behind you and let another party who have not prayed come and pray with you and let them take their precaution and their arms. Those who disbelieve wish that you would neglect your arms and your baggage so they could turn upon you in a single assault' (Surah an-Nisa, 4:102). This verse proves that one can perform Salat al-Khawf, and also shows how to perform it. (2) This hadith is evidence: 'Abdullah ibn Umar said: I went on an expedition with the Messenger of Allah [SAW] towards Najd, and we faced the enemy and formed ranks. The Messenger of Allah [SAW] stood to lead us in prayer. A party stood with him while another party faced the enemy. The Messenger of Allah [SAW] bowed with those with him and performed two prostrations, then they moved away...'
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that Salat al-Khawf (the prayer of fear) is permissible, but only under specific conditions: the presence of an enemy, or fear of drowning or burning. The author provides two proofs: first, the Quranic verse (4:102) which describes the method of prayer during battle, and second, a hadith from Ibn Umar narrating the practice of the Prophet. The Hanafi school considers this prayer as a concession for situations of extreme fear.

Key Terms
صلاة الخوف (salat al-khawf): The prayer performed in a state of fear, especially during battle or when facing danger.
وجه (wajh): Evidence or proof cited by the author to support the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What conditions make Salat al-Khawf permissible according to the Hanafi school?
A) Only in the presence of an enemy
B) In the presence of an enemy, or fear of drowning or burning
C) Only when there is fire
D) Only when in a state of travel

Key Takeaway
Salat al-Khawf is a permissible concession granted for situations of extreme fear, including enemy presence, drowning, and fire.

Salah — Prayer

The Hanafi Method of Salat al-Khawf When the Congregation Disputes Over the Imam
Explains the Hanafi procedure for Salat al-Khawf with disputed imam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi procedure for Salat al-Khawf when the congregation disputes over one imam, and identify the variant rak'ah distributions for two-, three-, and four-rak'ah prayers.

Core Idea
When the community cannot agree on an imam, the imam splits the congregation into two groups, leading each in part of the prayer while the other guards.

This passage addresses a practical scenario during battle or fear: the congregation cannot unite behind one imam. The Hanafi school, relying on prophetic practice, provides a structured solution. The imam divides the people into two groups: one group prays with the imam while the other faces the enemy, then they swap. The number of rak'ahs each group receives depends on the total rak'ahs of the prayer. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its evidences from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
Recognize that this ruling applies when there is disagreement over the imam; the procedure is permissible (ja'iz).
The ruling is not obligatory but a permissible method for Salat al-Khawf.
2
Understand the general procedure
The imam makes two groups: one group guards against the enemy while the other prays with the imam; then they exchange roles.
The guarding group faces the direction of the enemy, not the qibla.
3
Determine rak'ah distribution based on prayer length
For four-rak'ah prayers: the imam leads each group in two rak'ahs. For three-rak'ah (Maghrib): the first group prays two rak'ahs with the imam, the second group one. For two-rak'ah prayers: the imam leads each group in one rak'ah.
After the imam completes his prayer, each group completes their remaining rak'ahs individually.
4
Examine the Prophetic evidence
The ahadith from Ibn Umar, Jabir, and Ibn Mas'ud demonstrate the detailed method for different prayer lengths.
These ahadith are from Bukhari, Muslim, and Abu Dawud; their transmission is zanni.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۸۵۳) واذا تنازع القوم فى الصلوة خلف امام واحد فيجعلهم طائفتين واحدة بازاء العدو ويصلى مكان الطائفة التي لم تصل فجاء وا فركع رسول الله بهم ركعة وسجد سجدتين ثم سلم فقام كل واحد منهم فركع لنفسه ركعة وسجد سجدتين - ( بخارى شریف، ابواب صلوۃ الخوف، ص ۱۵۱، نمبر ۹۴۲ / ابوداؤد شریف ، باب من قال يصلى بكل طائفة رکعتة ثم يسلم، ص ۱۸۴، نمبر ۱۲۴۴)

وجه : (۱) دو گروہ کر کے نماز پڑھائے اس کی دلیل اوپر آیت اور حدیث دونوں میں گزری (۲) اور چار رکعت والی نماز ہو تو دو رکعت پہلی جماعت کو اور دو رکعت دوسری جماعت کو پڑھائے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن جابر قال اقبلنا مع رسول الله حتى اذا كنا بذات الرقاع ..... قال فنودی با لصلاة فصلى بطائفة ركعتين ثم تأخروا فصلى بالطائفة الاخرى ركعتين ، قال فكانت لرسول الله الا الله أربع ركعات و للقوم ركعتان . (مسلم شریف، باب صلاة الخوف ص ۳۴۰، نمبر ۱۹۴۹/۸۴۳ را بود او د شریف ، باب من قال یصلی بکل طائقہ رکعتین ، ص ۱۸۷، نمبر ۱۲۴۸)

(۳) اور دورکعت والی نماز ہو تو ہر جماعت کو ایک ایک رکعت پڑھائے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن مسعود قال صلى بنا رسول الله له صلاة الخوف فقاموا صفا خلف رسول الله الا الله و صف مستقبل العدو ، فصلى بهم رسول الله الله ركعة ، ثم جاء الآخرون فقاموا مقامهم و استقبل هؤلاء العدو فصلى بهم النبي الا الله ركعة ثم سلم فقام هؤلاء فصلوا لأنفسهم ركعة ثم سلموا ثم ذهبوا فقاموا مقام أولئك مسقبلى العدو و رجع أولئك الى مقامهم فصلوا لأنفسهم ركعة
(853) And when the people quarrel over praying behind one imam, he makes them into two groups: one facing the enemy, and he prays with the group that did not pray... Then they came and the Messenger of Allah [SAW] bowed with them one rak'ah and performed two prostrations, then he said salam. Then each of them stood and bowed for himself one rak'ah and performed two prostrations. (Bukhari, Hadith 942; Abu Dawud, Hadith 1244). Evidence: (1) The proof for dividing into two groups has been mentioned in the verse and hadith above. (2) And if the prayer is of four rak'ahs, he leads the first group in two rak'ahs and the second group in two rak'ahs. For this, there is the hadith of Jabir: ... (3) And if the prayer is of two rak'ahs, he leads each group in one rak'ah. For this, there is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: ...
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage addresses a scenario where the congregation cannot agree on praying behind a single imam. The imam divides them into two groups: one faces the enemy (or guards), and the other prays with him. The method depends on the number of rak'ahs in the prayer. For a four-rak'ah prayer, the imam leads each group in two rak'ahs; for a two-rak'ah prayer, each group gets one rak'ah; for Maghrib (three rak'ahs), the first group gets two and the second one rak'ah. The author cites ahadith to support these variations.

Key Terms
طائفتين (tāʾifatayn): Two groups into which the congregation is divided for Salat al-Khawf.
صلاة الخوف (ṣalāt al-khawf): The fear prayer performed during battle or danger, with abbreviated or split forms.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One rak'ah each
B) Two rak'ahs for the first group and one for the second
C) Two rak'ahs for each group
D) Three rak'ahs for the first and one for the second

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school provides a clear, prophetic-based procedure for Salat al-Khawf when the congregation cannot agree on an imam, ensuring the prayer is performed validly even under duress.

General Method of Salat al-Khawf Behind One Imam
Explains division into two groups and imam's action with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi method of Salat al-Khawf behind one imam and derive the number of rak'ahs per group using hadith proofs.

Core Idea
In Salat al-Khawf, the imam leads each group separately, and each group completes its prayer individually.

This lesson covers the general method of Salat al-Khawf (prayer of fear) when the entire congregation prays behind a single imam. It is a ruling with proof, where the author provides the practical method and supports it with hadith from Bukhari, Abu Dawud, Muslim, and the actions of the Prophet (peace be upon him). Understanding this method is essential for correctly performing the prayer in conditions of fear.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled? Salat al-Khawf behind one imam. The ruling is that it is valid (sahih) and follows the Sunnah.
The text does not declare it obligatory but prescribes method.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites multiple hadith: from Bukhari (narrated by a companion), Jabir's hadith for four-rak'ah prayers, and Ibn Mas'ud's for two-rak'ah prayers.
All are ahad hadith, so zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's actions in these hadiths are a practical demonstration (fi'l) which indicates the sunnah method for the prayer of fear.
Hanafi usul holds that the Prophet's fi'l indicates permissibility and method.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) have different methods, such as the imam praying two rak'ahs with each group for all prayers. Hanafi school relies on the method described.
Cross-madhhab ikhtilaf exists; our lesson focuses on Hanafi position.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The method is mufta bihi (relied upon) from the Zahir al-Riwayah. The text does not mention tarjih authority, but it is established in the school.
The method is operative for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلوة الخوف
(۸۵۳) واذا تنازع القوم فى الصلوة خلف امام واحد فيجعلهم طائفتين واحدة بازاء العدو ويصلى مكان الطائفة التي لم تصل فجاءوا فركع رسول الله بهم ركعة وسجد سجدتين ثم سلم فقام كل واحد منهم فركع لنفسه ركعة وسجد سجدتين - ( بخارى شریف، ابواب صلوۃ الخوف، ص ۱۵۱، نمبر ۹۴۲ / ابوداؤد شریف ، باب من قال يصلى بكل طائفة رکعته ثم يسلم، ص ۱۸۴، نمبر ۱۲۴۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ نماز خوف میں دو جماعتیں بنائے گا اور امام ہر جماعت کو ایک ایک رکعت پڑھائے گا۔ اور باقی ایک رکعت خود اپنے اپنے طور پر پڑھیں گے۔
ترجمه : (۸۵۳) جب ایک امام پیچھے نماز پڑھنے کے بارے میں قوم جھگڑا کرنے لگے، تو امام انکود وگروہ میں بانٹ دے، ایک دشمن کے مقابلے پر ہواور دسرے گروہ کو دورکعت نماز میں سے ایک رکعت پڑھائے اور چار رکعت والی نماز اور مغرب کی نماز میں سے دورکعت پڑھائے۔
تشریح : اگر قوم دو اماموں کے پیچھے نماز پڑھنا چاہتی ہے تب تو نماز خوف کی یہ شکل اختیار کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے ،لیکن اگر ایک ہی امام کے پیچھے پوری قوم نماز پڑھنا چاہتی ہے تو امام قوم کو دوگروہوں میں بانٹ دے، ایک گروہ کو پہلے نماز پڑھائے ، اور دوسرا گروہ دشمن کے سامنے کھڑا ر ہے، اگر دو رکعت والی نماز ہے، مثلا فجر کی نماز ہے تو پہلے گروہ کو ایک رکعت پڑھائے اور دوسرے گروہ کو دوسری رکعت پڑھائے۔ اور اگر چار رکعت والی نماز ہے، مثلا ظہر کی عصر کی ، اور عشاء کی نماز ہے تو پہلی جماعت کو دورکعت پڑھائے ، اور دوسری جماعت کو دوسری دو رکعت پڑھائے ، اور اگر مغرب کی نماز ہے تو پہلی جماعت کو دورکعت پڑھائے اور دوسری جماعت کو صرف ایک رکعت پڑھائے۔ وجه : (۱) دو گروہ کر کے نماز پڑھائے اس کی دلیل اوپر آیت اور حدیث دونوں میں گزری (۲) اور چار رکعت والی نماز ہو تو دو رکعت پہلی جماعت کو اور دو رکعت دوسری جماعت کو پڑھائے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن جابر قال اقبلنا مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم حتى اذا كنا بذات الرقاع ..... قال فنودی با لصلاة فصلى بطائفة ركعتين ثم تأخروا فصلى بالطائفة الاخرى ركعتين ، قال فكانت لرسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أربع ركعات و للقوم ركعتان . (مسلم شریف، باب صلاة الخوف ص ۳۴۰، نمبر ۱۹۴۹/۸۴۳ را بود او د شریف ، باب من قال یصلی بکل طائقہ رکعتین ، ص ۱۸۷، نمبر ۱۲۴۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ظہر عصر کی نماز ہو اور امام مقیم ہو تو ہر جماعت کو دو دو رکعت نماز پڑھائے ۔ (۳) اور دورکعت والی نماز ہو تو ہر جماعت کو ایک ایک رکعت پڑھائے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن مسعود قال صلى بنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم صلاة الخوف فقاموا صفا خلف رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم و صف مستقبل العدو ، فصلى بهم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ركعة ، ثم جاء الآخرون فقاموا مقامهم و استقبل هؤلاء العدو فصلى بهم النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ركعة ثم سلم فقام هؤلاء فصلوا لأنفسهم ركعة ثم سلموا ثم ذهبوا فقاموا مقام أولئك مستقبلى العدو و رجع أولئك الى مقامهم فصلوا لأنفسهم ركعة ر
Chapter of the Prayer of Fear. (853) And when the people dispute regarding praying behind one imam, he makes them two groups: one facing the enemy, and he prays with the group that has not yet prayed. The messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) came and prayed one rak'ah with them, performed two prostrations, then said salam. Then each of them stood and prayed one rak'ah for himself and performed two prostrations. (Bukhari, Abu Dawud). From this hadith it is understood that in the prayer of fear he will make two congregations and the imam will lead each congregation one rak'ah, and they will pray the remaining one rak'ah on their own. Translation: (853) When the people dispute about praying behind one imam, the imam should divide them into two groups, one facing the enemy, and he leads the other group one rak'ah from a two-rak'ah prayer, and two rak'ahs from a four-rak'ah prayer or Maghrib prayer. Explanation: If the people want to pray behind two imams, then there is no need to adopt this form of the prayer of fear. But if the entire people want to pray behind one imam, then the imam should divide them into two groups. He leads one group first, and the other group stands facing the enemy. If it is a two-rak'ah prayer, e.g., Fajr, he leads the first group one rak'ah and the second group the second rak'ah. If it is a four-rak'ah prayer, e.g., Zuhr, Asr, and Isha, he leads the first group two rak'ahs and the second group the other two rak'ahs. If it is Maghrib, he leads the first group two rak'ahs and the second group only one rak'ah. Evidence: (1) The proof for dividing into two groups is from the verse and hadith mentioned earlier. (2) For a four-rak'ah prayer, he leads the first group two rak'ahs and the second group two rak'ahs. For this there is the hadith from Jabir: We set out with the Messenger of Allah until we were at Dhat al-Riqa'... He said: The call to prayer was made, and he led one group in two rak'ahs, then they stepped back and he led the other group in two rak'ahs. He said: So the Messenger of Allah had four rak'ahs and the people had two rak'ahs. (Muslim, Abu Dawud). In this hadith, when it is Zuhr or Asr prayer and the imam is a resident, he leads each group two rak'ahs. (3) For a two-rak'ah prayer, he leads each group one rak'ah each. For this there is the hadith from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud: The Messenger of Allah led us in the prayer of fear. They stood in a row behind the Messenger of Allah and a row facing the enemy. He led them in one rak'ah, then the others came and took their place, and these faced the enemy. He led them in one rak'ah, then said salam. Then these stood and prayed one rak'ah for themselves, then said salam, then went and took the place of those facing the enemy, and those returned to their place and prayed one rak'ah for themselves.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof explaining the general method of Ṣalāt al-Khawf when the entire congregation prays behind a single imam. The text begins with a ruling (853) that if the people dispute about the prayer, the imam should divide them into two groups: one group faces the enemy while the other prays. The imam leads the group that has not yet prayed. The hadith from Bukhari and Abu Dawud is cited to show that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed one rak'ah with each group and then each person completed their prayer individually. The Urdu commentary elaborates that if the people wish to pray behind two imams, this method is not needed; but if they insist on one imam, this division is necessary. It explains the number of rak'ahs based on the prayer type: for two-rak'ah prayers (Fajr), each group gets one rak'ah; for four-rak'ah prayers (Zuhr, Asr, Isha), each group gets two rak'ahs; for Maghrib, the first group gets two and the second one rak'ah. The text then provides hadith proofs for the four-rak'ah case (hadith of Jabir) and for the two-rak'ah case (hadith of Ibn Mas'ud). The student should note that the first group does not complete its prayer immediately; it remains facing the enemy and completes later.

Key Terms
صلاة الخوف (ṣalāt al-khawf): The prayer performed during battle or when there is fear of enemy attack, with a specific method to ensure both prayer and security.
طائفة (ṭā'ifa): A group or portion of the congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Salat al-Khawf with one imam for a four-rak'ah prayer like Zuhr, how many rak'ahs does the imam lead for each group?
A) One rak'ah each
B) Two rak'ahs each
C) Three rak'ahs for first group, one for second
D) Full prayer for first group, then second group

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi method of Salat al-Khawf behind one imam divides the congregation into two groups, with the imam leading each group in part of the prayer, and each person completing their prayer individually.

Salah — Prayer
beginner

Detailed Steps for Completing Salat al-Khawf (854-858)
Procedural steps for Ṣalāt al-Khawf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sequence of actions for each group in Ṣalāt al-Khawf and explain why the imam says salam alone.

Core Idea
The imam completes his prayer alone; each group completes its missed rak'ahs later.

Ṣalāt al-Khawf is a special prayer performed under fear of attack. The following passage details the exact steps each group follows after the initial portion with the imam. Understanding these steps ensures the prayer is valid and maintains military vigilance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two groups
The first group prays the initial part with the imam, then goes to guard. The second group then joins the imam for the remaining rak'ahs.
Each group takes turns guarding and praying.
2
Determine the imam's actions after the second group
After leading the second group in the remaining rak'ahs, the imam says salam alone because his prayer is complete, even though the followers have not yet completed theirs.
The imam does not wait for the followers to finish.
3
Follow the sequence of each group completing their prayer
The second group goes to the enemy, then the first group returns and completes their prayer without recitation (as laḥiq), then the second group returns and completes with recitation if they wish.
The order ensures equality between groups.

Source Text

ترجمه : (۸۵۵) اور وہ دوسرا گر وہ آئے ، اور امام انکو جتنی باقی رہ گئی ہے وہ نماز پڑھائے، اور اکیلا سلام پھیر دے۔ تشریح : دوسرا گروہ امام کے پیچھے آئے اور جتنی رکعتیں باقی رہ گئیں ہیں وہ پڑھائے ، مثلا ظہر کی نماز ہے اور پہلے گروہ کو دو رکعت پڑھا چکے ہیں تو اب دوسرے گروہ کو باقی دو رکعت پڑھائے ، اور مغرب کی نماز ہے تو پہلے گروہ کو دورکعت پڑھا چکے ہیں اس لئے اب دوسرے گروہ کو ایک رکعت پڑھائے ، اور فجر کی نماز ہے اور پہلے گروہ کو ایک پڑھا چکے ہیں اس لئے دوسرے گروہ کو باقی ایک رکعت پڑھائے ۔ اب چونکہ امام کی نماز پوری ہو چکی ہے، اور مقتدی کی نماز بھی پوری نہیں ہوئی ہے اس لئے امام اکیلے سلام پھیر دے۔ان دونوں باتوں کے لئے حدیث او پر گزر چکی ہے۔
ترجمه : ( ۸۵۶) پھر یہ دوسرا گروہ دشمن کی طرف چلا جائے۔
تشریح : ایک صورت یہ ہے کہ دوسرا گر وہ لگے ہاتھ اپنی پہلی رکعت پڑھ لے اور نماز پوری کر کے سلام پھیر دے اور دشمن کی طرف جائے ، تا کہ نماز کی حالت میں آنا جانا بھی نہ پڑے اور نماز فاسد ہونے کا خطرہ بھی نہ رہے لیکن اس صورت میں پہلے گروہ کے ساتھ برابری نہیں رہے گی، کیونکہ اسکی نماز بھی پوری نہیں ہوئی ہے، اور دوسرے گروہ کی پوری ہوگئی یہ ٹھیک نہیں اس لئے اچھا یہ ہے کہ یہ ابھی نماز پوری نہ کرے پہلے گروہ کے بعد پوری کرے۔ اور اگر نماز پوری کر لی تب بھی جائز ہے۔

(854) And this group goes to the enemy walking. (855) And that (other) group comes, and he leads them in what remains, and he gives salam alone. (856) Then they go to the enemy. (857) Then they come and then they give salam. (Abu Dawud) From this hadith it is that he leads each group one rak'ah, and also that the first group, after completing their one rak'ah, or after completing two rak'ahs, will not say salam, but will go to face the enemy and complete their prayer later. Translation: (854) And this group goes to the enemy walking. Explanation: They go walking so that if there is an attack, the prayer will not break due to excessive action, and they cannot continue with the imam's prayer. Translation: (855) And that second group comes, and the imam leads them in what remains of the prayer, and he says salam alone. Explanation: The second group comes behind the imam, and he leads them in the remaining rak'ahs. For example, if it is Zuhr prayer and he has led the first group two rak'ahs, he now leads the second group the remaining two rak'ahs. If Maghrib, he led the first group two rak'ahs, so now he leads the second group one rak'ah. If Fajr, he led the first group one rak'ah, so now he leads the second group the remaining one rak'ah. Now since the imam's prayer is complete, and the followers' prayer is not complete, the imam says salam alone. The hadith for both these matters has passed earlier. Translation: (856) Then this second group goes to the enemy. Explanation: One scenario is that the second group immediately prays their first rak'ah and completes the prayer with salam and goes to the enemy, so that there is no coming and going during prayer and no risk of invalidating the prayer. But in this case, there will be no equality with the first group, because their prayer is not complete, while the second group's prayer became complete. That is not good. Therefore, it is better that they do not complete the prayer now; they complete it after the first group. And if they do complete it, it is also permissible. Translation: (857) Then the first group comes and completes their prayer without recitation and gives salam and goes to the enemy. Explanation: The first group's first rak'ah was behind the imam, so they are in the status of lahiq (one who catches up later), and as if the imam is present before them. Therefore, when this group comes, they complete the prayer without recitation and give salam, and then go to the enemy, so that the second group comes and completes their prayer. Translation: (858) Then the second group comes, if they wish, and completes the remaining prayer with recitation.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage contains a series of specific rulings (854-858) detailing the procedure after the initial portion of Ṣalāt al-Khawf. The text first states (854) that the first group (which has prayed with the imam) goes to face the enemy, and they walk to avoid excessive movement that might invalidate the prayer. (855) Then the second group comes, and the imam leads them in the remaining rak'ahs of the prayer. After that, the imam says salam alone because his prayer is complete but the followers still have to complete theirs. (856) Then the second group goes to the enemy. The commentary notes that it is better for the second group not to complete their prayer immediately, so that they have equal status with the first group who also have not completed. However, if they do complete it, it is also permissible. (857) Then the first group returns and completes their prayer without recitation (since they had already recited in the first rak'ah with the imam) and gives salam. (858) Finally, the second group comes and completes the remaining prayer with recitation if they wish. The hadith from Abu Dawud supports the overall method. The student should understand that the prayer is performed in such a way that each group takes turns praying with the imam and guarding, and each completes their prayer after the imam has finished.

Key Terms
لاحق (lāḥiq): A follower who has missed some part of the prayer with the imam and joins later, considered as still following the imam.
مشاة (mushātan): Walking, as opposed to running or other movements, to avoid invalidating the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He waits for the second group to complete their prayer and says salam with them
B) He says salam alone and then the second group completes their prayer
C) He does not say salam until the first group returns
D) He says salam and then leaves

Key Takeaway
The imam completes his prayer alone; each group completes its missed rak'ahs later, with the first group omitting recitation as laḥiq.

Salah — Prayer

Walking to the Enemy in Salat al-Khawf
Ruling on walking in Salat al-Khawf to prevent nullification of prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for the first group's movement in Salat al-Khawf and explain why walking on foot is required according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Walking on foot in Salat al-Khawf preserves the continuity of prayer by preventing excessive movement that would nullify it.

In the fear prayer (Salat al-Khawf), the commander divides the army into two groups. After completing the first rak'ah with the imam, the first group proceeds towards the enemy. But why must they go on foot? The Hanafi school provides a precise legal rationale rooted in the concept of 'amal kathir (excessive action) that can invalidate prayer. This lesson unpacks that ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State explicitly what the first group must do: they must proceed towards the enemy on foot after the first rak'ah with the imam. This is a mandatory action (wajib) for the validity of their prayer.
The ruling is part of the Hanafi method for Salat al-Khawf.
2
Understand the legal reason
Analyze the rationale: walking minimizes movement. If they ran or made excessive movements, an attack might force them to engage in actions that constitute 'amal kathir (three or more consecutive movements), which would nullify the prayer.
Walking keeps them within the bounds of permissible movement in prayer.
3
Connect to 'amal kathir
Define 'amal kathir as per Hanafi fiqh: any three consecutive movements of a limb. Recognizing that walking involves minimal, controlled steps helps students see why it avoids nullification.
The threshold for 'amal kathir is specific to the Hanafi school.
4
Recognize the context
Place this ruling within Salat al-Khawf: the first group remains followers (muqtadi) of the imam even when physically distant. They are considered lahiq (those still following the imam). Thus, preserving the prayer condition is crucial.
The group does not exit the prayer; they continue as followers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۸۵۴) وتمضى هذه الى العدو مشاة (۸۵۴) اور یہ گر وہ چلتے ہوئے دشمن کے مقابلے پر جائے۔ تشریح : چلتے ہوئے دشمن کے مقابلے پر اس لئے جائے کہ اگر وار ہوگا تو عمل کثیر کی وجہ سے نماز ٹوٹ جائے گی اور امام کی نماز کے ساتھ بنا نہیں کر سکے گا۔
(854) And this group goes to the enemy on foot. (854) And this group goes walking to face the enemy. Explanation: It goes walking to face the enemy because if an attack occurs, the prayer would break due to excessive action, and [the one attacked] cannot continue with the imam's prayer.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage states a ruling: after praying the first rak'ah (or two in a four-rak'ah prayer) with the imam, the first group proceeds towards the enemy on foot. The reason given in the commentary is that if they were attacked, the necessary defensive movements would constitute 'amal kathir (excessive action), which nullifies prayer. Walking minimizes such movement and allows them to remain in the state of prayer as followers (muqtadi) of the imam, because they are considered 'lahiq' (those who are still following the imam though physically distant). This ruling is part of the Hanafi method for Salat al-Khawf.

Key Terms
عمل کثیر (amal kathir): Excessive physical movement that nullifies prayer according to the Hanafi school
صلاۃ الخوف (salat al-khawf): The fear prayer performed during battle or imminent danger, with shortened and modified form

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

The Second Group in Salat al-Khawf: Imam's Role and Salam
Ruling on the second group joining the imam for the remaining rak'ahs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi procedure for the second group in Salat al-Khawf and explain why the imam says salam alone.

Core Idea
Imam says salam alone because his prayer is complete; the second group is masbuq and completes later.

In the fear prayer, the congregation is split into two groups for security. After the first group has prayed part of the prayer, the second group replaces them. This lesson explains what the imam does with the second group and why he finishes his prayer alone, leaving the followers to complete their missed rak'ahs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Understand that this applies to Salat al-Khawf, where the imam first prays some rak'ahs with the first group, then the second group approaches.
The number of rak'ahs already prayed depends on the prayer type.
2
Determine the remaining rak'ahs
Calculate how many rak'ahs are left for the imam to pray with the second group based on what was prayed with the first group.
Example: Zuhr (4 total) – if 2 prayed with first, remain 2; Maghrib (3) – if 2, remain 1; Fajr (2) – if 1, remain 1.
3
Recognize the imam's completion
The imam prays the remaining rak'ahs with the second group, completing his own prayer obligation. He then says salam alone.
The imam does not wait for the second group to finish their missed rak'ahs.
4
Understand the followers' status
The second group becomes masbuq (latecomers) – they still owe the rak'ahs they missed from the first part. They must complete their prayer individually after the imam's salam.
This is because their prayer is not yet complete.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۸۵۵) وجاءت تلک فصلی بهم ما بقى وحده (۸۵۵) اور وہ دوسرا گر وہ آئے ، اور امام انکو جتنی باقی رہ گئی ہے وہ نماز پڑھائے، اور اکیلا سلام پھیر دے۔ تشریح : دوسرا گروہ امام کے پیچھے آئے اور جتنی رکعتیں باقی رہ گئیں ہیں وہ پڑھائے ، مثلا ظہر کی نماز ہے اور پہلے گروہ کو دو رکعت پڑھا چکے ہیں تو اب دوسرے گروہ کو باقی دو رکعت پڑھائے ، اور مغرب کی نماز ہے تو پہلے گروہ کو دورکعت پڑھا چکے ہیں اس لئے اب دوسرے گروہ کو ایک رکعت پڑھائے ، اور فجر کی نماز ہے اور پہلے گروہ کو ایک پڑھا چکے ہیں اس لئے دوسرے گروہ کو باقی ایک رکعت پڑھائے ۔ اب چونکہ امام کی نماز پوری ہو چکی ہے، اور مقتدی کی نماز بھی پوری نہیں ہوئی ہے اس لئے امام اکیلے سلام پھیر دے۔
(855) And that second group comes, and the imam prays with them what remains alone. (855) And that second group comes, and the imam prays with them the remaining [rak'ahs] and says salam alone. Explanation: The second group comes behind the imam, and he prays with them the remaining rak'ahs. For example, if it is Zuhr prayer and he has already prayed two rak'ahs with the first group, then he prays the remaining two rak'ahs with the second group. If it is Maghrib and he has prayed two with the first, he prays one with the second. If Fajr and he prayed one with the first, he prays the remaining one with the second. Now since the imam's prayer is complete, but the followers' prayer is not yet complete, the imam says salam alone.

Commentary
This ruling describes the second stage: after the first group leaves, the second group approaches and prays behind the imam. The imam prays the remaining rak'ahs of the prayer with them, depending on what was already prayed with the first group. The imam then says salam alone because his prayer is finished, while the followers still owe rak'ahs (they are masbuq) and will complete on their own later.

Key Terms
مسبوق (masbuq): One who joins the imam later and misses one or more rak'ahs; here the second group is masbuq because they joined after the first rak'ahs

Second Group's Completion in Fear Prayer
Ruling on the second group proceeding to the enemy after praying with imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two options for the second group in Salat al-Khawf and identify the preferred method according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
In fear prayer, the second group may complete immediately or later; maintaining parity is preferred.

After the first group completes their prayer with the imam, the second group must decide when to finish their remaining rak'ah. This passage outlines two permissible sequences: immediate completion followed by engagement, or engagement first and later completion. Both are valid, but the preferred method preserves equality (barabari) between the groups in the duration of prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Recognize that the ruling concerns the second group after they have prayed one rak'ah with the imam and the first group has left.
The second group is still in a state of prayer but not yet complete.
2
List the two options
Option A: Complete the missed rak'ah immediately and then go to the enemy. Option B: Go to the enemy first and complete the prayer later after the first group returns.
Both are permissible (mubah).
3
Understand the preference
The preferred method is to delay completion because it maintains equality (barabari) between the two groups in terms of when they finish praying.
Immediate completion would result in the second group having completed while the first group remains incomplete.
4
Note the ruling
The text states that immediate completion is valid (ja'iz) but 'better' (behtar) to delay.
The term 'better' indicates mustahabb (preferred), not wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۸۵۶) فذهبوا الى العدو (۸۵۶) پھر یہ دوسرا گروہ دشمن کی طرف چلا جائے۔ تشریح : ایک صورت یہ ہے کہ دوسرا گر وہ لگے ہاتھ اپنی پہلی رکعت پڑھ لے اور نماز پوری کر کے سلام پھیر دے اور دشمن کی طرف جائے ، تا کہ نماز کی حالت میں آنا جانا بھی نہ پڑے اور نماز فاسد ہونے کا خطرہ بھی نہ رہے لیکن اس صورت میں پہلے گروہ کے ساتھ برابری نہیں رہے گی، کیونکہ اسکی نماز بھی پوری نہیں ہوئی ہے، اور دوسرے گروہ کی پوری ہوگئی یہ ٹھیک نہیں اس لئے اچھا یہ ہے کہ یہ ابھی نماز پوری نہ کرے پہلے گروہ کے بعد پوری کرے۔ اور اگر نماز پوری کر لی تب بھی جائز ہے۔
(856) So they go to the enemy. (856) Then this second group goes towards the enemy. Explanation: One scenario is that the second group immediately completes their first rak'ah, finishes the prayer, says salam, and then goes to the enemy, so that coming and going does not occur during prayer and there is no risk of invalidating the prayer. But in this scenario, equality with the first group will not be maintained, because the first group's prayer is not complete while the second group's is complete—this is not proper. Therefore, it is better that they do not complete now but complete after the first group [returns]. But if they do complete, it is also permissible.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage discusses the second group's movement after praying with the imam. They have two options: either complete their missed rak'ah immediately and then go to the enemy, or go first and complete later. The preferred (mustahabb) method is to go to the enemy first and complete after the first group returns, to maintain parity between the groups. However, completing immediately is also permissible.

Key Terms
برابری (barabari): Equality between the two groups in the duration of prayer completion

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The second group in Salat al-Khawf may choose either order, but the preferred method is to go to the enemy before completing the prayer to maintain equal duration with the first group.

First Group in Fear Prayer: Completion Without Recitation
Ruling on completion without recitation for the first group in fear prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why the first group in Salat al-Khawf completes their prayer without recitation and identify the concept of lahik.

Core Idea
A lahik completes prayer without recitation because the imam is still considered present.

This lesson examines a specific ruling in the fear prayer (Salat al-Khawf). The first group, after returning from the front line, completes their remaining rak'ah(s) without recitation. Understanding the Hanafi concept of 'lahik' is key to grasping why they do not recite, distinguishing them from those who join the prayer late (masbuq).

Guided Path
1
Identify the groups and their roles
In Salat al-Khawf, the imam leads one group (the first group) in one rak'ah, while a second group stands guard. The first group then leaves for the front, and the second group comes to complete their prayer with the imam.
2
Recognize the lahik status of the first group
Upon returning, the first group is considered lahik (لاحق). A lahik is one who joined the imam initially but missed part of the prayer due to a legitimate interruption (here, fighting). Their prayer remains attached to the imam, as if he is still present.
Lahik is distinct from masbuq (مسبوق), who joins after the imam has started and recites when completing.
3
Apply the ruling: no recitation required
Because the imam is considered present for the lahik, the first group completes their remaining rak'ah(s) without reciting the Quran. They then say salam and proceed to the front to relieve the second group.
This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school; other schools may require recitation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاولى واتموا بلا قراءة وسلموا ومضوا (۸۵۷) پھر پہلا گروہ آئے اور اپنی نماز بغیر قرآت کے پوری کرے اور سلام پھیر دے اور دشمن کی طرف چلا جائے تشریح : پہلے گروہ کی پہلی رکعت امام کے پیچھے ہوئی ہے اس لئے وہ لاحق ہے، اور گویا کہ اس کے سامنے امام موجود ہے اس لئے جب یہ گروہ آئے تو بغیر قرآت کے نماز پوری کرے اور سلام پھیر دے اور اس کے بعد دشمن کے سامنے جائے ، تاکہ دوسرا گروہ آکر اپنی نماز پوری کرے۔
The first group, and they complete without recitation, say salam, and go. (857) Then the first group comes and completes their prayer without recitation, says salam, and goes to the enemy. Explanation: The first rak'ah of the first group was behind the imam, so they are lahik, and it is as if the imam is present before them. Therefore, when this group comes, they complete the prayer without recitation, say salam, and then go to the enemy, so that the second group can come and complete their prayer.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This ruling explains that the first group, upon returning to the prayer place, completes their remaining rak'ah(s) without recitation because they are lahik (followers whose imam is still considered present). They are not required to recite the Quran because they were originally following the imam. They say salam and then immediately proceed to the enemy to relieve the second group, who then come and complete their own prayer.

Key Terms
لاحق (lahiq): A follower who missed part of the prayer but remains connected to the imam; here the first group is lahik because their prayer is still attached to the imam

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Second Group Recitation in Salat al-Khawf
Ruling on the second group's completion with qira'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for the second group's completion in Salat al-Khawf and explain why recitation is wajib for them.

Core Idea
The second group, as masbuq, must recite Quran when completing their prayer.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the fear prayer (Salat al-Khawf). The second group, having missed part of the prayer with the imam, are considered masbuq. The text gives them discretion in location but mandates recitation. Understanding this requires distinguishing between lahiq and masbuq in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize that this ruling applies to Salat al-Khawf with two groups. The first group prayed one rak'ah with the imam, then exchanged with the second group.
2
Locate the ruling
The text states that the second group may complete their prayer wherever they wish (at their guard post or at the imam's place) and that they complete it 'with recitation' (bi qira'ah).
Discretion in location does not apply to the obligation of recitation.
3
Explain the reason
The second group is masbuq because they missed the first rak'ah(s) with the imam. They must recite because the imam's recitation does not cover their missed rak'ahs.
Contrast with the first group (lahiqa) who follow the imam without reciting in the first two rak'ahs.
4
Apply the classification
In Hanafi fiqh, the masbuq recites in the completion (qada) of missed rak'ahs. This is wajib (obligatory) for the second group.
If they omit recitation, the completion is still valid but they must perform sajdah al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) if deliberate, or repeat if missed unintentionally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم جاءت الاخرى ان شاء واصلوا ما بقى بقرائة (۸۵۸) پھر دوسرا گر وہ آئے اگر چاہے اور باقی نماز قرآت کے ساتھ پوری کرے۔ تشریح : دوسرا گروہ چاہے تو وہیں نماز پوری کرے جہاں وہ کھڑا ہے، اور چاہے تو امام کی جگہ پر آئے اور اپنی باقی نماز پوری کرے۔ اور اس گروہ کی پہلی رکعت چھوٹی ہے اس لئے یہ مسبوق ہے اس لئے یہ اپنی باقی نماز قرآت کے ساتھ پوری کرے۔
Then the other group comes, if they wish, and complete what remains with recitation. (858) Then the second group comes, if they wish, and complete the remaining prayer with recitation. Explanation: The second group may complete the prayer wherever they stand, or they may come to the imam's place and complete. Since they missed the first rak'ah, they are masbuq, so they complete the remaining with recitation.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage gives the second group discretion to complete their prayer either where they were guarding or at the prayer place. Because they are masbuq (they missed the first rak'ah/s), they must recite Quran (al-Fatiha and a sura) in their completion, unlike the first group who were lahik.

Key Terms
مسبوق (masbuq): One who missed one or more rak'ahs with the imam; here the second group is masbuq
قرائة (qira'ah): Recitation of the Quran, specifically al-Fatiha and a sura, during prayer

Extreme Fear Prayer: Individual Mounted Prayer with Gestures
Ruling on extreme fear prayer with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for prayer in extreme fear and identify the three proofs cited.

Core Idea
In extreme fear, pray individually on a mount with gestures in any direction – the only requirement is presence of mind.

When fear reaches a level that even the two-group prayer is impractical, the Hanafi school permits a fully individual prayer on a horse or any mount. The worshipper performs gestures (ima') for bowing and prostrating, and may face any direction. This concession is based on the Quranic verse and prophetic practice, as explained below.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Identify that this concerns the prayer (salah) in extreme fear (shiddat al-khawf). The ruling is permissible (mubah) due to necessity.
This is a concession, not the default practice.
2
Locate the dalil
Three proofs are cited: Quran 2:239, a hadith from Bukhari via Ibn Umar, and an athar from Ibn Sirin.
The Quranic verse is the primary evidence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Each proof supports the ruling: Quran gives general permission for prayer on foot or riding; hadith explicitly mentions praying standing and riding; athar confirms gestures in any direction.
The combination of proofs establishes the full scope of concessions.
4
Note the conditions
Conditions for this concession: extreme fear (shiddat al-khawf) such that congregation is difficult, inability to dismount, and the prayer is performed individually (furada).
If fear is less severe, the two-group prayer is preferred.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, one prays individually on the mount, using gestures for ruku and sujud, with no requirement to face qiblah.
This applies to both fard and nafl prayers in this situation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان اشتدّ الخوف صلوا ركبانا فرادى بالايماء الى اى جهة قدروا (۸٥۹) اور جب خوف زیادہ سخت ہو تو اکیلے سواری پر اشارہ سے جدھر ہو سکے نماز پڑھ لے۔ تشریح دشمن سامنے ہے اور خوف اتنا ہے کہ جماعت کے ساتھ نماز پڑھنا مشکل ہے تو سواری پر رہتے ہوئے نماز پڑھے جس طرح نفل نما ز سواری پر پڑھتے ہیں، اس صورت میں قبلہ رخ ہونا بھی ضروری نہیں سواری کا رخ جدھر ہواسی طرف ہو کر نماز پڑھ لے وجه : (۱) اس کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے ۔ افان خفتم فرجالا او رکبانا - ( آیت ۲۳۹، سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں ہے کہ خوف ہو تو سواری پر نماز پڑھ سکتے ہیں۔ اور اس کے مطابق تمام رعایتیں مل جائیں گی (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عمر نحو من قول مجاهد اذا اختلطوا قياما و زاد ابن عمر عن النبي علم و ان كانوا اكثر من ذالك فليصلوا قياما و رکبانا ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب صلاة الخوف رجالا ور کہا نا ص ۱۵۱، نمبر ۹۴۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ سواری پر نماز پڑھی جاسکتی ہے (۳) عن ابن سيرين انه كان يقول في صلوة المسايفة يومى ايماء حيث كان وجهه _(مصنف ابن ابى شيبة ۴۶ ۷ فی الصلاة عند المسایفة ، ج ثانی، ص ۲۱۵، نمبر ۸۲۶۷) اس اثر میں موجود ہے کہ جس جانب چہرہ متوجہ ہو اسی جانب اشارہ کر کے نماز پڑھے گا۔
And when fear becomes intense, they pray riding, individually, with gestures, in whatever direction they are able. (859) And when fear is extremely intense, one prays alone on a ride, with gestures, in whatever direction possible. Explanation: The enemy is present and fear is such that praying in congregation is difficult; then one prays while riding, just as one prays voluntary prayers on a ride. In this case, facing the qiblah is not necessary; one prays in the direction the ride is facing. Proof: (1) The evidence is this verse: 'If you fear, then [pray] on foot or riding' (Quran 2:239). This verse indicates that when there is fear, one may pray on a ride, and all concessions are granted accordingly. (2) Hadith: From Ibn Umar, similar to the saying of Mujahid: 'When they mix [in battle], standing.' And Ibn Umar added from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'And if they are more than that, they pray standing and riding.' (Bukhari, Book of Salat al-Khawf, Chapter: Prayer on foot and riding, p. 151, no. 943) (3) From Ibn Sirin, he would say about the prayer of combat: he gestures with his face wherever his face is directed. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, vol. 2, p. 215, no. 8267)
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with multiple proofs. It addresses the most extreme level of fear (shiddat al-khawf) where even the two-group method is impractical. The Hanafi ruling permits praying individually (furada) on horseback (or any ride) with gestures (ima') in any direction, even without facing qiblah. The commentary explains that this follows the same rule as nafl prayers on a ride. Three proofs are cited: (1) Quran 2:239, (2) a hadith from Bukhari via Ibn Umar, (3) an athar from Ibn Sirin. These establish the full range of concessions for extreme fear.

Key Terms
ايما (ima'): Gesture with head or body indicating bowing and prostration, used in prayer when unable to do full movements

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum requirement for prayer in extreme fear according to this passage?
A) Face qiblah and bow fully
B) Pray in congregation with two groups
C) Pray individually on a ride with gestures in any direction
D) Pray on foot without moving

Key Takeaway
In extreme fear, the only essential for prayer is intention and gestures; all other elements (direction, full movements, congregation) are waived.

Condition for Valid Fear Prayer: Enemy Presence Required
Condition for validity of fear prayer: enemy must be present

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for the validity of the special fear prayer and explain why enemy presence is necessary.

Core Idea
The special fear prayer is only valid when an enemy is present — otherwise, its concessions are not permitted.

This lesson examines a specific condition for the validity of Salat al-Khawf. The ruling is concise: the special form that permits walking and turning from qiblah is conditional upon the actual presence of an enemy combatant. Without that necessity, normal prayer rules apply.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act being ruled upon is the special form of Salat al-Khawf (fear prayer) as described — involving walking and turning from qiblah. The ruling is that it is not valid without a condition.
2
Recognize the condition for validity
The condition is the presence (hudur) of an enemy ('aduww). This is a shart (condition) external to the prayer itself that must be met for this special form to be permissible.
The condition is not the danger itself, but the presence of an enemy combatant.
3
Understand the rationale behind the condition
The commentary explains that this prayer form includes actions that normally invalidate prayer (walking, turning from qiblah). These concessions are allowed only due to necessity caused by enemy presence. Without that necessity, the actions remain prohibited.
This shows the principle that necessity (darura) permits normally prohibited actions.
4
Apply the condition to scenarios
In real life, a Muslim performing Jumu'ah or other prayers in a combat zone may use this form only when enemy is present. If the enemy is not present (e.g., natural disaster, non-combat threat), the normal prayer rules apply without these concessions.
If unsure, the default is to pray normally; the special form is an exception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم تجز بلا حضور عدو (٨٦٠) اور یہ نماز دشمن کے حاضری کے بغیر جائز نہیں ہے۔ تشریح : اس نماز میں آدمی کونماز کے درمیان ہی چلنا پڑتا ہے، قبلہ سے رخ پھرتا ہے، اس لئے دشمن ہو تب ہی یہ نماز جائز ہے ورنہ نہیں۔
And it is not valid without the presence of an enemy. (860) And this prayer is not permissible without the presence of an enemy. Explanation: In this prayer, one has to walk during prayer and turn away from the qiblah, so only if there is an enemy is this prayer valid; otherwise not.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This ruling states a condition: the specific form of Salat al-Khawf (with walking and turning) is only valid when an enemy is present (hudur 'aduww). The commentary explains that because this prayer involves actions that would normally invalidate prayer (moving, turning from qiblah), these concessions are only allowed due to necessity. Without the enemy, these actions are not permitted, and the normal rules of prayer apply.

Key Terms
حضور عدو (hudur 'aduww): The physical presence of an enemy (non-Muslim combatants) that necessitates fear prayer
صلاة الخوف (salat al-khawf): Fear prayer; a special form of prayer performed in times of battle or enemy attack, allowing certain modifications for safety.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Enemy presence
C) Travel
D) Congregation

Key Takeaway
The special fear prayer is conditional upon the presence of an enemy; without it, the concessions of walking and turning from qiblah are not permitted, and normal prayer rules apply.

The Recommendation to Carry Weapons During Fear Prayer
Ruling with Quranic proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on carrying weapons during fear prayer and identify the Quranic evidence that supports this ruling.

Core Idea
Carrying weapons during fear prayer is mustahabb, not obligatory, based on the Quranic instruction to take arms.

In times of battle or danger, the lawgiver has allowed certain measures to maintain security even during worship. This lesson examines the specific ruling on carrying weapons while performing the fear prayer (Salat al-Khawf). The source text presents the Hanafi position that it is recommended (mustahabb) to have one's weapon on the body, and the evidence from Quran 4:102. We'll explore the proof and the reasoning behind the recommendation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is carrying weapons during prayer when in a state of fear. The ruling is mustahabb (recommended). Note that the text uses 'yustahabb' (it is recommended).
The Arabic word 'mustahabb' is synonymous with 'sunnah' in this context.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites Quran 4:102, which describes the fear prayer and includes the instruction 'let them take their weapons'. This verse serves as the primary evidence.
The verse is partially quoted; the full verse continues with the second group's actions.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'walya'khudhu' (let them take) indicates a command. In Hanafi usul, a command (amr) normally indicates obligation, but here it is interpreted as recommendation due to the context of permissible self-defense during a vulnerable act like prayer.
The ruling is mustahabb despite the imperative form, because the primary objective is the prayer itself, and the weapon is a precaution.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Hanafi position is that it is recommended. Other schools may view it as obligatory or merely permissible. The text does not elaborate on the ikhtilaf, but the cross-madhhab status is marked as mukhtalaf fih.
5
Summarize the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that carrying weapons is mustahabb. If the weapon is impure, it must be cleaned. This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text

ويستحب حمل السلاح في الصلوة عند الخوف (٨٦١) خوف کے وقت میں نماز میں ہتھیار اٹھانا مستحب ہے۔ تشریح : خوف ہو تو جو ہتھیار جسم پر باندھا ہوا ہے اس کے ساتھ نماز پڑھنا مستحب ہے ا کہ حملہ ہوتو بر وقت مقابلہ کیا جا سکے۔ البتہ اگر تلوار وغیرہ میں ناپا کی ہو تو اس کو صاف کر لیا جائے۔ وجه : (۱) اس آیت میں ہتھیار اٹھانے کی ترغیب ہے۔ واذا كنت فيهم قاقمت لهم الصلوة فلتقم طائفة منهم معك وليأخذوا اسلحتهم فاذا سجدوا فليكونوا من ورائكم ولتأت طائفة اخرى لم يصلوا فليصلوا معك

Explanation: If there is fear, it is recommended to pray with the weapon that is strapped on the body, so that if an attack occurs, one can counter it in time. However, if the sword etc. has impurity on it, then it should be cleaned. Proof: (1) This verse encourages carrying weapons: 'When you are among them and stand to lead them in prayer, let a group of them stand with you and let them take their weapons. When they prostrate, let them be behind you. Let another group come who have not yet prayed and let them pray with you.'
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This final ruling covers the recommendation (istihbab) of carrying weapons during Salat al-Khawf. The commentary explains that the weapon should be already strapped on the body to allow quick defense. If the weapon is ritually impure (najis), it must be cleaned. The proof is Quran 4:102, which is the same verse that outlines the two-group method and mentions taking weapons. This Quranic text explicitly includes the instruction to take arms, establishing the recommendation.

Key Terms
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended act, omission is not sinful but rewarded if done
صلاة الخوف (Salat al-Khawf): Fear prayer, a shortened form of prayer performed during battle or danger.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Two Groups in Salat al-Khauf
Rulings for the two groups in the prayer of fear

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings for the two groups in salat al-khauf and explain why the second group recites while the first does not.

Core Idea
In Salat al-Khauf, the first group leaves without recitation; the second group, as masbuq, recites the remainder.

Salat al-Khauf (the prayer of fear) has special rulings to accommodate the needs of soldiers facing the enemy. The passage presents two groups: the first group, after one rak'ah with the imam, completes their prayer without recitation and departs, while the second group joins the imam later and, being masbuq, must complete their remaining rak'ah with recitation. Understanding these rulings requires parsing the roles of each group and the reasoning behind the recitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two groups
The first group prays one rak'ah with the imam, then completes their prayer without recitation, says salam, and leaves to guard. The second group comes later, prays one rak'ah with the imam (their second rak'ah), and then completes the remaining rak'ah on their own.
The first group's prayer is valid despite missing recitation.
2
State the ruling for the first group
The first group completes without recitation (no qira'ah) and says salam. This is because they are in a state of guarding the congregation, and necessity allows dropping recitation.
Recitation is normally wajib, but here it is omitted due to fear.
3
State the ruling for the second group
The second group is considered masbuq (latecomer) because they missed the first rak'ah. They must complete their remaining rak'ah with recitation.
As a masbuq, they follow the imam in what they catch and complete the missed rak'ah after imam's salam.
4
Explain the difference in recitation
The first group does not recite because their prayer is shortened due to the necessity of guarding. The second group recites because they are completing a full prayer as a masbuq.
The first group's omission of recitation is specific to salat al-khauf; normally it would invalidate the prayer.
5
Note the optional location for completion
The commentary states that the second group may complete their prayer either at their current spot or come to the imam's place. Both are permissible.
This flexibility accommodates the battlefield situation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلوة الخوف الاولى واتموا بلا قراءة وسلموا ومضوا (858) ثم جاءت الاخرى ان شاء واصلوا ما بقى بقرائة (859) تشریح : دوسرا گروہ چاہے تو وہیں نماز پوری کرے جہاں وہ کھڑا ہے، اور چاہے تو امام کی جگہ پر آئے اور اپنی باقی نماز پوری کرے۔ اور اس گروہ کی پہلی رکعت چھوٹی ہے اس لئے یہ مسبوق ہے اس لئے یہ اپنی باقی نماز قرآت کے ساتھ پوری کرے۔
Chapter of the Prayer of Fear: The first group completes without recitation and says salam and departs. Then the other group, if they wish, completes the remaining with recitation. Commentary: The second group, if it wishes, may complete the prayer where it is standing, and if it wishes, may come to the imam's place and complete the rest of its prayer. And the first rak'ah of this group is missed, so it is a latecomer (masbuq); thus it should complete the rest of its prayer with recitation.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings for the prayer of fear (salat al-khauf). The first ruling: The first group of soldiers, after praying one rak'ah with the imam, completes their prayer without recitation (since they are guarding), says salam, and departs to face the enemy. The second ruling: The second group then prays with the imam, but since they missed the first rak'ah, they are considered latecomers (masbuq) and must complete their remaining rak'ah with recitation. The commentary clarifies that the second group has a choice: they can either complete the prayer at their current position or come to the imam's place. The key point is that the first group does not recite because they are in a state of guarding, not because the prayer is invalid without recitation.

Key Terms
مسبوق (masbuq): A person who joins the congregation after the imam has already started, missing one or more rak'ahs.
صلاة الخوف (salat al-khauf): The prayer performed in a state of fear, especially during battle, with specific rulings to facilitate prayer while facing the enemy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) They recite the remaining rak'ah and then depart.
B) They depart without reciting and say salam.
C) They wait for the second group to finish.
D) They join the second group.

Key Takeaway
In Salat al-Khauf, the first group prays without recitation due to guarding, while the second group, as masbuq, completes the missed rak'ah with recitation.

Prayer in Extreme Fear on Mounts: Ruling and Proofs
Ruling for extreme fear prayer with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for prayer in extreme fear on mounts, identify the three proofs cited, and apply the conditions for this concession.

Core Idea
Extreme fear permits prayer on mounts with gestures, even without facing qiblah — a divine concession.

When fear becomes so intense that even the normal prayer of fear (salat al-khauf) cannot be performed, the Shari'ah provides an even greater concession: you may pray alone on your mount, using gestures (ima') for ruku' and sujud, and you may face any direction. This lesson examines the ruling, its conditions, and the textual proofs that establish it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and its hukm level. The act is performing obligatory prayer in extreme fear while riding, gesturing in any direction. The hukm level is mubah (permissible) as a concession.
This is a rukhsah (concession), not an azimah (original ruling).
2
Locate the proofs (dalil)
Find the three proofs cited in the passage: Quran 2:239, a hadith from Bukhari (no.943), and an athar from Ibn Sirin. Identify each dalil type: Quran is qati al-thubut, hadith is zanni, athar is zanni.
The Quranic verse is the primary evidence; the hadith and athar support and clarify.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does each proof lead to the ruling? The verse uses the imperative in a context of fear, indicating permission to pray on foot or riding. The hadith explicitly mentions praying standing and riding. The athar shows gesturing wherever one's face is directed.
The imperative is understood as permissive here due to the context of hardship.
4
Check for ikhtilaf
Is there disagreement on any part? The cross_madhhab_status is mukhtalaf_fih; some scholars differ on whether facing the qiblah is completely waived. The Hanafi position is that it is waived in extreme fear.
This ikhtilaf does not affect the core permissibility.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the Zahir al-Riwayah transmissions from Imam Muhammad. The mufta bihi is that this concession is valid. No contrary strong evidence overrides it.
The evidence is consistent and the ruling is well-established.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان اشتدّ الخوف صلوا ركبانا فرادى بالايماء الى اى جهة قدروا (860) ترجمه : (859) اور جب خوف زیادہ سخت ہو تو اکیلے سواری پر اشارہ سے جدھر ہو سکے نماز پڑھ لے۔ تشریح دشمن سامنے ہے اور خوف اتنا ہے کہ جماعت کے ساتھ نماز پڑھنا مشکل ہے تو سواری پر رہتے ہوئے نماز پڑھے جس طرح نفل نماز سواری پر پڑھتے ہیں، اس صورت میں قبلہ رخ ہونا بھی ضروری نہیں سواری کا رخ جدھر ہواسی طرف ہو کر نماز پڑھ لے وجه : (1) اس کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے ۔ افان خفتم فرجالا او ركبانا - ( آیت 239، سورۃ البقرۃ 2) اس آیت میں ہے کہ خوف ہو تو سواری پر نماز پڑھ سکتے ہیں۔ اور اس کے مطابق تمام رعایتیں مل جائیں گی (2) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عمر نحو من قول مجاهد اذا اختلطوا قياما و زاد ابن عمر عن النبي علم و ان كانوا اكثر من ذالك فليصلوا قياما و رکبانا ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب صلاة الخوف رجالا ور کہا نا ص 151، نمبر 943) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ سواری پر نماز پڑھی جاسکتی ہے (3) عن ابن سيرين انه كان يقول في صلوة المسايفة يومى ايماء حيث كان وجهه _(مصنف ابن ابى شيبة 46 7 في الصلاة عند المسایفة ، ج ثاني، ص 215، نمبر 8267) اس اثر میں موجود ہے کہ جس جانب چہرہ متوجہ ہو اسی جانب اشارہ کر کے نماز پڑھے گا۔
And if fear intensifies, they pray on mounts individually with gesture towards any direction they are able. Translation: When fear becomes very severe, pray alone on a mount with gesture in whatever direction possible. Commentary: The enemy is in front and fear is such that praying in congregation is difficult, so pray while remaining on the mount just as one prays supererogatory prayer on a mount. In this case, facing the qiblah is not necessary; pray in the direction the mount is facing. Proofs: (1) The evidence is this verse: 'If you fear, then (pray) on foot or riding' (2:239). This verse indicates that when in fear, one can pray on mounts and all concessions apply. (2) Hadith: From Ibn Umar similar to the statement of Mujahid: 'When they mingle, standing...' and Ibn Umar added from the Prophet: 'And if they are more than that, let them pray standing and riding.' (Bukhari, chapter of Salat al-Khauf, men and riding, p.151, no.943). This hadith indicates that prayer on mounts is permissible. (3) From Ibn Sirin: 'He used to say regarding the prayer of warfare (musayafah): he gestures with his head wherever his face is directed.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, vol.2, p.215, no.8267). This report indicates that one gestures in the direction the face is turned.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling for prayer in extreme fear, where the danger is so great that even the normal prayer of fear is not possible. The ruling permits praying individually on mounts (or riding animals) with gestures (ima') instead of the full bowing and prostration, and facing any direction. The commentary explains that this is similar to how one prays supererogatory prayers on a mount, and even facing the qiblah is not required. Three pieces of evidence are provided: first, Quran 2:239, which gives a general permission for prayer on foot or riding; second, a hadith from Bukhari narrated by Ibn Umar; third, an athar from Ibn Sirin. These proofs establish the validity of this concession. Note that this prayer is only for extreme fear; in lesser fear, the normal two-group prayer is used.

Key Terms
إيماء (ima'): Gesture or nodding of the head in place of bowing (ruku') and prostration (sajdah) when unable to perform them fully.
ركبانا (rukbanan): Riding; praying while mounted on an animal or vehicle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In extreme fear, obligatory prayer is valid with gestures on a mount without facing qiblah, based on Quran, Hadith, and Athar.

Condition for Salat al-Khauf: Enemy Must Be Present
Condition for validity: presence of enemy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for the validity of salat al-khauf and explain why enemy presence is necessary.

Core Idea
Salat al-khauf is valid only when an enemy is present – the concessions require the emergency.

The prayer of fear (salat al-khauf) is a special dispensation that allows actions normally invalidating prayer, such as walking or turning from the qiblah. However, this dispensation is not unconditional. The decisive condition is the actual presence of a hostile enemy. Without that threat, the prayer must be performed in the normal manner. In this lesson, we examine that condition and its underlying rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its condition
Locate the phrase 'without the presence of an enemy' (بلا حضور عدو). The text explicitly states that the prayer is not permissible (لم تجز) in that case. This is the key condition of validity.
The condition is external to the prayer itself (shart), not an integral (rukn).
2
Understand the rationale for the condition
The commentary explains that during salat al-khauf, a person may need to walk and turn away from the qiblah – actions that would normally invalidate prayer. These concessions are only granted because of the necessity imposed by enemy presence.
This shows that the condition is not arbitrary but tied to the very nature of the prayer's allowances.
3
Distinguish from normal prayer and other dispensations
Compare with travel concessions: for example, qasr (shortening) is allowed on a journey regardless of enemy presence. Salat al-khauf is unique because it permits more severe deviations, and thus requires a greater necessity.
Many students mistakenly think salat al-khauf is allowed whenever one is afraid, even without an actual enemy.
4
Apply the condition to a scenario
Consider a situation where Muslims are on guard duty in a safe area but anticipate enemy arrival. Are they allowed to pray salat al-khauf? According to this text, no – the enemy must be present, not merely anticipated.
The Hanafi school is strict: the enemy must be in sight or posing an immediate threat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم تجز بلا حضور عدو (861) ترجمه : (860) اور یہ نماز دشمن کے حاضری کے بغیر جائز نہیں ہے۔ تشریح : اس نماز میں آدمی کونماز کے درمیان ہی چلنا پڑتا ہے، قبلہ سے رخ پھرتا ہے، اس لئے دشمن ہو تب ہی یہ نماز جائز ہے ورنہ نہیں۔
And it is not permissible without the presence of an enemy. Translation: And this prayer is not permissible without the presence of the enemy. Commentary: In this prayer, a person has to walk during the prayer, turns away from the qiblah, so this prayer is only valid when there is an enemy; otherwise not.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage states a crucial condition for the validity of the prayer of fear (salat al-khauf): the actual presence of an enemy. The commentary explains why: during this prayer, the worshiper may need to walk, turn away from the qiblah, and perform other actions that would normally invalidate the prayer. These concessions are only granted because of the necessity of facing the enemy. If there is no enemy, one must pray in the normal manner. Thus, the prayer of fear is a specific dispensation for wartime, not for general travel or other situations.

Key Terms
عدو (aduww): Enemy; in this context, a hostile force that poses a real threat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Salat al-khauf is only valid when an enemy is present; the concessions of walking and turning from qiblah are emergency allowances that do not apply otherwise.
