Tayammum for the Deceased: Mahram and Khuntha Mushkil
Ruling on tayammum when a mahram is present and for a khuntha mushkil.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on tayammum when a mahram is present and for a khuntha mushkil, and explain the reasoning behind the precautionary approach.

Core Idea
Tayammum replaces ghusl when mahram is present; for khuntha mushkil, tayammum is safer.

In preparing the deceased for burial, the general rule is that men wash men and women wash women. However, what if the only available person is a mahram relative? And what about a person of ambiguous gender (khuntha mushkil)? This lesson addresses these two specific cases, providing clear rulings based on the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling for mahram
The text states: if a mahram relative is present, he performs tayammum without cloth. Recognize that 'dhu rahm mahram' refers to a relative with whom marriage is permanently forbidden.
Mahram examples: father, brother, son, uncle from father's side, etc.
2
Understand why tayammum is allowed for mahram
Because a mahram can touch the deceased's body without obstacle, the tayammum can be performed directly, without a cloth barrier.
3
Identify the scenario and ruling for khuntha mushkil
The text says: for the khuntha mushkil, the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) is to perform tayammum. 'Khuntha mushkil' means a person whose gender is ambiguous, not clearly male or female.
4
Explain the reasoning for khuntha mushkil
Since the gender is unknown, it is uncertain whether a man or woman should wash the body. Tayammum is the precautionary measure to avoid a potential sin of touching the opposite gender improperly.
The commentator notes that it is better to pour water over a cloth covering the body.
5
Note the preferable opinion
Although the apparent narration says tayammum, the commentator suggests that pouring water over a cloth is better (ahsan). This is a tarjih within the Hanafi school.
The mufta bihi is tayammum in the apparent narration, but the better opinion is to pour water over cloth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان وجد ذو رحم محرم يُمّم بلا خرقة وكذا الخنثى المشكل يمّم فى ظاهر الرواية. (۸۸۹) ترجمه (۸۸۸) ہاں اگر کوئی محرم ہوتو بلا کپڑے کے تیتم کرادے۔ اور ایسے ہی خلشی مشکل کو تیم کرائے ۔ ظاہر روایت میں یہ ہے تشريح : اگر کوئی ذی رحم محرم مرد ساتھ ہو تو کپڑے کے بغیر بھی تیتم کراسکتا ہے، کیونکہ اس کے لئے ہاتھ لگانا جائز ہے۔ خلشی مشکل نہ مرد میں اس کا شمار ہے اور نہ عورت میں اس لئے اس کو مرد نسل دے یا عورت غسل دے یہ فیصلہ کرنا مشکل ہے، اس لئے اس کو بھی تیم کرا کر دفن کر دے، یہ ظاہر روایت ہے۔ بہتر یہ ہے کہ اس کو کپڑے کے اوپر سے پانی بہادے۔
And if there is a mahram relative, he performs tayammum without cloth. Similarly, for the khuntha mushkil, tayammum in the apparent narration. Translation (888): Yes, if there is a mahram, he performs tayammum without cloth. And similarly for the khuntha mushkil, tayammum in the apparent narration. Explanation: If a male mahram relative is present, he can perform tayammum without cloth, because it is permissible for him to touch. The khuntha mushkil is not counted as male nor female, so it is difficult to decide whether a man or woman should wash him; therefore, he is also given tayammum and buried. This is the apparent narration. It is better to pour water over him through a cloth.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This is a ruling statement: When a mahram relative (such as a father, son, brother, etc.) is present, he can perform tayammum directly without a cloth, because touching is allowed. For the khuntha mushkil (a person of ambiguous gender), since it is unclear whether they are male or female, the safe approach is to perform tayammum on them, as in the zahir al-riwayah. However, the commentator suggests that it is better to pour water over a cloth covering them.

Key Terms
ذو رحم محرم (dhu rahm mahram): A relative of the opposite gender with whom marriage is permanently prohibited.
خنثى مشكل (khuntha mushkil): A person with ambiguous genitalia, making it unclear whether they are male or female.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How is a khuntha mushkil to be prepared for burial according to the apparent narration?
A) A man washes him.
B) A woman washes her.
C) He is given tayammum.
D) He is left without washing.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum replaces ghusl for a deceased person when a mahram is present or when the deceased is a khuntha mushkil, ensuring modesty and avoiding uncertainty.

Permissibility of Washing a Young Child by Opposite Gender
Ruling on washing a child who has not reached the age of desire.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on washing a deceased child of the opposite gender and identify the condition that makes it permissible.

Core Idea
A man may wash a young girl and a woman a young boy if the child has not reached desire.

In funeral rites, washing the deceased (ghusl al-mayyit) is a communal obligation. This lesson addresses a specific question: when can a man wash a deceased girl, or a woman wash a deceased boy? The ruling hinges on the child's age and absence of sexual desire.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is washing a deceased child by a person of the opposite gender. The ruling (hukm) is permissible (mubah), not obligatory.
2
Identify the condition
The permissibility depends on the child having not reached the age of sexual desire (lam yashtahiyā). This is generally before puberty, around age 10-12.
Once a child reaches puberty, the ruling changes to prohibition for opposite gender.
3
Understand the rationale
Children below the age of desire are not considered objects of sexual attraction, so the usual gender segregation rules for washing the deceased are relaxed.
4
Apply to a scenario
If a 6-year-old boy dies and only adult women are available, it is permissible for a woman to wash him. Similarly, a man may wash a young girl.
Always confirm the child's age or lack of puberty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۸۸۹) ويجوز للرجل والمرأة تغسيل لم يشتهيا ترجمه : (۸۸۹) مرداور عورت دونوں کے لئے جائز ہے کہ ایسے بچے یا بچی کونسل دے جو شہوت کی حد تک نہ پہونچے ہوں تشریح : جوڑ کا یالڑ کی بالغ نہ ہوئے ہوں تو وہ بچہ کے درجے میں ہیں اس لئے انکومر بھی غسل دے سکتا ہے اور عورت بھی غسل دے سکتی ہے۔
(889) It is permissible for a man and a woman to wash (a child) who has not reached desire. Translation (889): For a man and a woman, it is permissible to perform ghusl for such a boy or girl who have not reached the age of desire. Explanation: If a girl or boy have not reached puberty, they are in the category of children, so a man can wash them and a woman can also wash them.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This is a concise ruling: It is permissible for a man to wash a young girl and for a woman to wash a young boy, as long as they have not reached the age where sexual desire becomes apparent (i.e., before puberty). The rationale is that children are not yet objects of desire.

Key Terms
لم يشتهيا (lam yashtahiyā): Children who have not reached the age of sexual desire, i.e., before puberty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is it permissible for a man to wash a deceased girl?
A) When she is his mahram.
B) When she has not reached the age of desire.
C) When there is no woman available.
D) It is never permissible.

Key Takeaway
A child who has not reached the age of desire can be washed by either gender.

Kissing the Deceased is Permissible (Mubah)
Ruling on kissing the deceased with proof from the Sunnah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kissing the deceased and identify the dalil from the Sunnah that supports it.

Core Idea
Kissing the deceased is mubah in the Hanafi school, proven by Abu Bakr's act recorded in Sahih al-Bukhari.

This passage clarifies a common misconception about impurity after death. Although some may feel repulsion, the Shari'ah has not prohibited it; rather, the action of the greatest companion provides clear evidence. Let us examine the proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is kissing the deceased. The author states 'لا بأس' (no harm), making it mubah (permissible) in the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari: Abu Bakr kissed the Prophet after his death, as narrated by Aisha and Ibn Abbas.
Hadith reference: Bukhari, Bab marad al-nabi wa wafatihi, no. 4455
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The act of Abu Bakr, witnessed by the Companions without any objection, indicates that kissing the deceased is permissible. The legal principle is that acts of the Companions in the presence of the Prophet (after his death, but during the period of the Companions) are evidence of permissibility unless explicitly prohibited.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some may argue kissing the deceased is makruh due to the impurity of death. The Hanafi response: the body of a Muslim is legally pure after death, as affirmed by the Shari'ah.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is permissibility (mubah), following the hadith evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۸۹۰) ولا بأس بتقبيل الميت ترجمه : (۸۹۰) میت کو بوسہ دینے میں کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے۔ تشریح : موت کے بعد اگر چہ ایک قسم کی کراہیت ہو جاتی ہے لیکن شرعی طور پر جسم پاک ہے اس لئے بوسہ لینے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے وجه : (۱) عن عائشة و ابن عباس ان ابا بكر قبل النبي الله عليه وسلم بعد موته . (بخاری شریف، باب مرض النبی و وفاته ص ۷۵۷، نمبر ۴۴۵۵ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضرت ابو بکر نے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا بوسہ لیا۔
(890) There is no harm in kissing the deceased. Translation (890): There is no objection in kissing the deceased. Explanation: After death, although there is a kind of dislike, but legally the body is pure, so there is no harm in kissing. Evidence: (1) From Aisha and Ibn Abbas that Abu Bakr kissed the Prophet peace be upon him after his death. (Sahih al-Bukhari, Book of the Prophet's illness and death, p. 757, no. 4455) This hadith shows that Abu Bakr kissed the Prophet.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof: Kissing the deceased is permissible and not disliked despite the general impurity of death. The proof is the action of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq kissing the Prophet after his death, as recorded in Sahih al-Bukhari. The commentator notes that although the body of a deceased person may be considered impure in some ways, legally it is pure.

Key Terms
تقبيل (taqbil): Kissing the deceased, which is permissible in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the evidence for the permissibility of kissing the deceased?
A) A verse from the Quran.
B) The action of Abu Bakr kissing the Prophet after his death.
C) A consensus of the companions.
D) An analogy with living people.

Key Takeaway
Kissing the deceased is permissible in the Hanafi school based on the established action of Abu Bakr in Sahih al-Bukhari.
